Tianjin and Beijing Abolish Native Opium Shops 91

Beiping Correspondence: When Song Zheyuan was in charge of Chahar Province, he established a Clearance Office in Chahar Province to handle the prohibition of opium. Ten opium shops (called "Da Yan") were established, with a certain amount of tax stamps affixed to each tael of opium, implementing public sales of native opium and promoting it to the Beijing-Tianjin area of Hebei Province. During transportation, soldiers of the 29th Army were dispatched to protect it. Promotional agencies were established in Beijing, Tianjin, and other places. The military expenses of the 29th Army were mostly allocated from this income. Since the establishment of the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Commission, Chairman Song Zheyuan specifically cited the precedent of Chahar Province and appointed Qi Wei to organize the Beijing-Tianjin Clearance Office in Beijing. All relevant opium prohibition regulations were based on the original ones in Chahar Province, modified in light of the local conditions in Beijing and Tianjin. The office was officially established on January 12th. At the same time, a Tianjin Office was established in Tianjin to handle all matters. All organs such as the Hebei and Beijing-Tianjin Opium Prohibition Supervision Office and the Opium Prohibition Committee Inspection Office were immediately abolished, and their files were taken over by the office. According to Qi Wei, "The main purpose of the office's opium prohibition is to implement strict prohibition and suppression measures in three steps. The first step concerns highly addictive drugs (such as heroin, morphine, Jindan, etc.), which will be absolutely and strictly prohibited. The second step concerns narcotic drugs (such as opium), which will be prohibited within a time limit, and will be carried out through methods such as persuasion (for non-smokers under 30), compulsory detoxification (for smokers over 30), and the establishment of detoxification hospitals, suppressing private opium smuggling, and restricting commercial operations. The third step is to implement strict prohibition when the time limit in the second step expires." Since its establishment, the office has successively promulgated four types of regulations: "Implementation Rules for Suppressing Private Sales and Restricting Commercial Operations," "Opium Prohibition Rules," "Provisional Regulations for the Management of Pharmacies and Drugstores," and "Tax Regulations." In February, it began soliciting merchants to operate opium shops. The capital for the establishment of a pharmacy must be at least 50,000 yuan. The capital for drugstores is divided into Grade A: 6,000 yuan, Grade B: 3,000 yuan, Grade C: 1,500 yuan, and Grade D: 800 yuan. In addition, it is also necessary to pay deposit, special permit fees, business license fees, and other items. The opium sold in pharmacies in Beijing mostly comes from the Ping-Sui, Ping-Han, and along the routes, as well as Shaanxi, Gansu, Ningxia, and Suiyuan. The Clearance Office stipulates regulations according to the situation in various places and the distance of the journey, affixing tax stamps of 10 cents to 50 cents for each tael of opium. Most of the opium in drugstores comes from pharmacies. As of the regulation time, about ten pharmacies and nearly a hundred drugstores have been established in Beijing and Tianjin. After the establishment of pharmacies and drugstores, in order to seek unified management, the office set up checkpoints in the four suburbs of Beijing, as well as at various stations, airports, and postal inspection offices, dispatching investigators, inspectors, and undercover agents to be stationed separately to inspect passing passengers and mail, and announced to opium smugglers to register and affix tax stamps for selling opium within a time limit. Anyone who violates the regulations and sells or carries opium privately will have the opium confiscated and stored in the public treasury established by the office. The offenders will be sent to the Pacification Commissioner's Office for interrogation. Since the implementation of public sales of opium in Beijing and Tianjin, due to the special local environment, large-scale private drug trafficking organizations established by Japanese and Korean ruffians are everywhere, and the authorities cannot prohibit them, resulting in a huge impact on opium shops. According to the regulations, opium in shops must be sold only after tax stamps have been affixed, and it is not allowed to open lights to serve customers. Opium addicts must also be sold opium based on permits. However, opium shops in Beijing and Tianjin, due to the impact of private foreign trafficking organizations, have poor business and have behaviors that violate the regulations, such as selling private drugs, opening rooms to serve customers for smoking, and selling drugs to opium addicts without permits, in order to attract customers. For this reason, the Clearance Office has negotiated with the Japanese side to ban Japanese and Korean private trafficking organizations, but the result is still ineffective. Recently, in order to seek its own interests, the office pretends not to know about the violations of the regulations by the shops and allows them to do whatever they want without restriction."

Xiao Zhenying, the Mayor of Tianjin, heard that the Beijing-Tianjin Clearance Office's performance in prohibiting opium was not good, and that opium shops had behaviors that violated the regulations, and expressed his dissatisfaction. He had proposed to abolish the Clearance Office or replace the director Qi Wei. It was finally decided to abolish all opium shops in both places first, and then discuss other issues. As for whether the agency that replaces the shops to sell opium will be operated by the government, Qi Wei and others are currently discussing it in Tianjin. The section chiefs of the office in Beijing have been meeting for days to discuss the progress of the office and various measures to deal with current affairs. It is said that the office may change its organization. Regarding the anti-smuggling part, the Investigation Office has been abolished since the 4th, and the Inspection and Undercover Offices have been merged. As for the other departments, they are currently under study. (May 5th)

Songjiang Guerrilla Team Solves Robbery Case in Songjiang 92

Zhang Yougen's house in Nantang Township, the seventh district of Punan, was robbed at midnight on the 30th of last month. Now, Zhao Zanchen, the commander of the bandit suppression guerrilla detachment, has investigated and arrested three bandits, Zhang Fujin, Monk Gu, and Zheng Zuogen, in Qijiadun, according to his second squadron's third platoon leader, Lü Zhongfu. A gun and 17 bolts of cloth were seized in the bandits' den. They confessed that they were the stolen goods from Zhang Yougen's house. Yesterday, Commander Zhao submitted a document to the district headquarters to send the bandits for interrogation. The 17 bolts of cloth seized in the case have been notified to the victim Zhang Yougen to come to the headquarters to claim them. At the same time, the team was ordered to strictly pursue the escaped bandits.

Haizhou: Yangxu Pilot Cotton Planting Farm 93

The area of Yangxu outside Dongdou in this county has more than a thousand hectares of wasteland. Because the soil is saline, it cannot grow rice or wheat. It only grows weeds every year, which is a pity to abandon. Now, Xu Xiangsheng from this county believes that the saline soil is most suitable for cotton planting. He specially introduced a Nantong cotton merchant to Haizhou a few days ago to lease 15 hectares of Yang's family wasteland in Yangxu. Starting this year, a pilot cotton planting farm will be established there, with a temporary six-year contract. If it can be successful, it will be gradually promoted.

Suzhou: Verdict in the Murder Case of Police and Security Personnel in Nanhui 94

Sun Yaoshan, the chief of the sixth sub-bureau of the Public Security Bureau of Zhangjiazai, Nanhui County, patrol officer Gan Xuehui, patrolman Zhu Qiutian, head of the fourth district Yu Feng (on bail), head of the security corps Sun Zhaoming (on bail), assistant staff member of the district office Sun Xunbai (on bail), members of the security corps Qian Baiwu and Yang Baoru, were accused of shooting and killing Zhu Alan, who was privately selling military equipment, on the night of July 17th last year. The case was transferred to the Wuxian District Court for trial, which pronounced its verdict at 3 pm yesterday (the 6th). Sun Zhaoming was sentenced to life imprisonment for instigating murder and deprived of political rights for life. Sun Xunbai, Sun Yaoshan, Yu Feng and others were sentenced to life imprisonment for jointly instigating murder and deprived of political rights for life. Gan Xuehui, Zhu Qiutian, Qian Baiwu, Yang Baoru and others were sentenced to 15 years imprisonment for jointly committing murder and deprived of political rights for ten years. The defendants were dissatisfied with the verdict and planned to appeal to the Jiangsu High Court.

Wuxi: Resolution of the Disturbance Caused by the Blocking of Pujiqu Bridge 95

Residents in the Sanliqiao area of Beitang in Xiyi recently complained that the river water there had turned black and smelled bad. They had previously sent a letter to the First District Office, which forwarded it to relevant factories around Wuqiao East and West, such as Lixin Dyeing and Weaving Factory, Xiexin Woolen Mill, and Liyong Paper Mill, asking them to improve the water discharge equipment. The Xin Yun Inspection Team and the County Government's Construction Bureau and Public Security Bureau also went to inspect. Lixin had already changed the water pipe to the inner bay and blocked the bay mouth. Xiexin had also added a water purification pool to store and release sewage. However, the water still smelled bad recently. On the afternoon of the 4th, residents in the area rushed to the Beitang Town Office to request a solution, but no solution was found. They then carried the flags of the Public Health Corps and rushed to the Pujiqu Bridge riverbank, filling the river with sand, mud, stones, yellow stones, and broken bricks to build a dam. The persuasion of the Fifth Sub-bureau of the Public Security Bureau was ineffective, and they continued to block the river on the 6th. Chen Yuchu, the Director of the Public Security Bureau, personally went to dissuade them, and they stopped in the afternoon. However, the area is a vital transportation route between Chengxi and urban and rural areas. Once it is blocked, the public is panicked. Yesterday morning, the County Government specially convened an emergency meeting with the directors of the Public Security and Construction Bureaus, the director of the First District, the mayor of Beitang Town, and the County Chamber of Commerce to decide to order the mayor of Beitang Town to first restore the river transportation and to have the Construction and Public Security Bureaus jointly investigate the source of the black water and find ways to improve it. The disturbance was finally resolved.

Jiangyin: Tianzhang Silk Store Goes Bankrupt Due to Losses 96

The Tianzhang Silk and Satin Store on Dongda Street in the city has been in operation for 12 years since Gu Muyong took over. Business was usually good and credit was also good. Various deposits amounted to more than 40,000 yuan. In recent years, affected by rural bankruptcy, the price of goods has fallen, and profits have been eroded, resulting in a tight turnover. The store owner Gu Muyong was unable to maintain it. He left for Shanghai a few days ago. On the 5th, he sent a fast letter to Lu Zhongling, the person in charge of the store, Lin Songming of the Silk and Cloth Association, etc., stating that he was in Shanghai and was going to commit suicide by jumping into the sea in Gaoqiao, with losses of more than 30,000 yuan, and that the business would be closed for settlement. In the afternoon, depositors rushed to withdraw their deposits or cut out goods. The partners were not authorized to make decisions and dispersed in the evening. The store's inventory was sealed by the association. The Chamber of Commerce will hold a meeting on the 6th to discuss the handling method.

Gaoyou: Farmer Hangs Himself Due to Lack of Rice Seeds 97

The eighth district of this county has suffered another spring famine this year. It suffered a hail disaster the day before yesterday. Xu Dixian, a farmer near Xixiang Township, committed suicide by hanging himself in his room on the night of the 2nd because of various shortages, no items to pawn, no way to borrow money, and difficulty in life. His family found him dead in the morning of the 3rd.

Jiaxing: Sericulture in the Four Suburbs is Approaching 98

Sericulture in the four suburbs of Jiaxing is approaching. This year, due to the cold weather, some of the silkworm eggs distributed by the guidance centers in various districts have not been able to hatch, causing the villagers to argue with the distribution centers. As a result, the silkworm harvest this year is scarce. The early batch is currently in the first molt. Due to the weather, the molting is uneven. It is expected that the silkworm harvest will be much less. As for the leaf market, the sprouts are not growing well, and the leaf pulp is not thick. In addition, the price of mulberry leaves has been cheap for years, so many mulberry trees have been dug up and planted with other crops. The land this year is actually less than in previous years. As a result, the price of leaves has risen. In the past two or three days, the selling price per dan has risen from more than 50 cents to about 70 cents. According to insiders, if the weather is good and the sericulture is good, the price of leaves will definitely rise again, but it will not be as expensive as in the previous years. Silk merchants are registering with the Silkworm Silk Control Association to prepare for cocoon collection. However, due to the issue of mixed collection (cocoon merchants plan to collect both local and improved varieties in each factory), they are still arguing.

Ningbo: Truth About the Double Corpse Case in Zhenhai 99

Regarding the case of the discovery of two floating corpses of young men and women outside the Nanmen Gate in Zhenhai, the reporter went to Zhenhai to investigate the truth in order to understand the truth. The main cause of death of the deceased is as follows: Ge Shengjie from Gejia, Zhuangqiao, Cixi, is sixty years old. His wife is Ms. So-and-so. His mother is still alive. He has seven children. The family is reunited and has not yet separated. His son, Qi Min, married Sheng Jinmei, the second daughter of the Sheng family in the area, five years ago. They were very loving and had a three-year-old son. However, Qi Min was honest by nature and had many misfortunes. Therefore, he was often depressed. Last year, through the introduction of relatives and friends, he went to work as a partner in the Yifeng Herbal Medicine Bank in Shanghai. However, Qi Min's income was very small and he could not take care of his family. His grandmother, Ms. So-and-so, was very snobbish and discriminated against Qi Min and his wife, treating them differently from other granddaughters-in-law, and often criticized them. Therefore, the relationship between the sisters-in-law was not very harmonious. His father, Shengjie, often ordered him to subsidize the family. Qi Min was in such an environment, truly a case of crying and laughing, and he was always at fault. Therefore, the thought of being tired of the world arose. Last month, Jinmei received an invitation from her sister's husband in Shanghai to stay in Shanghai for a short time. Qi Min also went to visit. The sisters met and confided in each other, deeply feeling that the future was bleak and the heart to be tired of the world was more decisive. Qi Min drafted three suicide notes, addressed to relatives, embraced his son and took his wife, falsely claiming to go out, and took a boat to Zhenhai. Walking to Qingshui Pu, they threw the child into the river center. The husband and wife tied each other together and jumped into the river at the same time. The child's body was discovered in Qingshui Pu on the morning of the 27th. The bodies of the man and woman were washed by the tide and discovered in Lianzi Daotou the day before yesterday.

From Huainan Road to Chaoxian County 101

— Jiewen

Huainan Coal Mine Produces 1,500 to 1,600 Tons Daily; Huainan Railway Transports with Utmost Agility

Huainan Coal Mine was initially a privately-run enterprise, producing approximately 700 to 800 tons of coal daily. Since the National Government's Construction Committee took over, five additional mines have been successively opened, increasing daily output to as much as 1,500 to 1,600 tons. Subsequently, for transportation convenience, the Huainan Railway was built from Tianjia'an in Huaiyuan County within the mining area, passing through Hefei and Chaoxian County, directly reaching Yuxi Town on the Yangtze River opposite Wuhu, traversing western Anhui for a length of 220 kilometers. After its completion in January of this year, not only could coal be rapidly transported to the Yangtze River within a day, transferred by steamship to be sold in Nanjing, Shanghai, Jiujiang, Wuhan, and other places, but also the transportation in various counties of central Anhui has greatly benefitted from it. I recently visited the road and also visited the famed Xianren (Immortal) Cave in Chaoxian County, known throughout Anhui, with no known end. I record my impressions as follows:

Pilgrimage to Yuxi Town: The Huainan Road starts from Huaiyuan, passes through Hefei, Chaoxian County, and Hanshan, ending in Wuhu. Its transportation importance relates not only to commerce and culture. To facilitate joint transport with the Jiangnan Company's Nanjing-Wuhu Road, a ferry terminal was specially set up on the Yangtze River in Wuhu, equipped with ferries to transport passengers. I departed at dawn on the 2nd, and the ferry took 40 minutes. Upon landing, since it was not yet time for the train to depart, I lingered briefly in Yuxi. In the past, Yuxi was a major hub for sailing vessels in central Anhui, with a forest of masts, creating a majestic scene. Hence, past warlords and politicians all regarded the customs posts and transit taxes of this town as lucrative positions. However, no one cared about construction. Now that Huainan Road has its terminal station here, the station, warehouses, and ferry terminals are being actively constructed. A small-scale power plant has been completed and is already providing electricity. Technical engineers, laborers, and small businesses, such as restaurants and stalls, that have sprung up in response, number no fewer than several thousand. The future prosperity and importance of Yuxi can be foreseen.

What I Saw in the Third and Fourth Class Cars: I boarded the train at 8:30 AM. In addition to two third-class passenger cars, there were as many as seven or eight fourth-class cars for the poor. The rest were open coal cars, mostly empty. Except for a small amount of goods like bamboo brooms, the fourth-class cars were packed with overflow passengers, standing for long distances, exposed to wind and sun. Although there were only two third-class cars, the total number of passengers was less than ten. The economy, frugality, and resilience of the rural people can be seen here. The dining car business cannot be promoted because of this. A pot of tea costing five cents might only be bought by one or two passengers in third class. Bread, eggs, and rice are only frequently purchased on Nanjing-Shanghai trains. The carriage arrangement is similar to other lines. However, the porters are not trained and move awkwardly, lacking vitality. The authorities of the road seem to need to pay attention to this point. Starting from Tianjia'an Station and reaching Wuhu Terminal, the route passes through Datong, Huainan Mining, Shuijiahu, Zhuxiang, Xiatangji, Luoji, Shuangdunji, Hefei, Cuozhen, Qiaotouji, Jiongyanghe, Zhonghan, Chaoxian County, Lintou, Dongguan, Tongchengzha, Shenjiaxiang, and Yuxikou, for a total of twenty stations. The journey takes a total of ten hours and thirty-five minutes. From Yuxi to Chaoxian County, it only takes three hours and twenty-eight minutes. In the past, traveling between Wuhu and Chaoxian only relied on small boats, requiring departure in the morning and arrival at dusk. The roadbed throughout the entire route is extremely solid and uses heavy-duty steel rails. Therefore, the train travels smoothly, unlike the Nanjing-Wuhu section of the Jiangnan Company, which is like sitting on a ship at sea, making people uncomfortable. It takes ten years to grow trees, but willows easily provide shade. The willows planted along the roadside are expected to become a forest in three years, providing natural protection for the roadbed.

Chaoxian County: Small Town with Green Mountains. Chaoxian County has been famous for a long time in history, formerly known as Nanchao. Tang the Successful imprisoned Jie here. The county town is only seven li in circumference, surrounded by mountains and water, exuding an ancient charm. The streets are paved with stone, so there is no mud even in heavy rain. The newly built asphalt roads are not as naturally clean. Although the houses are mostly old, each has the beauty of gardens. Therefore, the annual value of flower production within Chaoxian town alone has reached over 100,000 yuan, not counting other plums and loquats. Chaoxian crabapples have long been famous for their color and taste. However, wealthy families regard them as a type of ornamental plant, and no effort is made to increase production, which is a great pity. Woniu Mountain in the city originally had many flowers, fruits, and trees. Last year, with the donation of Zhang Zhizhong from the Central Military Academy, it was developed into Niu Mountain Park. "A small town cradles a green mountain" captures the poetic richness of Chaoxian's scenery. Looking far from the mountain, surrounded by thousands of mountains, one can see a corner of Chaohu Lake. The lake spans hundreds of miles, with the water and sky merging into one color, boundless. Aquatic products are abundant, but there is no method for unified production, capture, and sale. Because it is freshwater, the fish and shrimp are delicious and without a fishy smell. The whitebait is particularly outstanding, as white as silver, without scales or bones. There are plans to can it for export, which is a type of industry.

The Depth and Distance of Xianren Cave. Chaoxian County is originally located in the midst of thousands of mountains. Silver Screen Mountain, Phoenix Flag Mountain, Lion Mountain, and Cloth Drum Mountain all possess natural beauty. "Mountains surround Chaoxian" is a true depiction of Chaoxian County. The reason why I made Chaoxian County my destination on this trip was actually attracted by Xianren Cave and the peony on the cliff of Silver Screen Mountain. The mountain is about forty li from the city. Young boys and girls lead donkeys to greet tourists outside the north gate at a very low price. Riding in the deep mountains and green fields is like being in a painting. The interest is something that city people cannot imagine. Every time we joyfully sing, the mountains echo, and only in the realm of nature can this true beauty and true joy be found. After more than two hours, we arrived at the foot of the cliff. Looking up, the cliff is dozens of zhang high. A peony plant grows upside down in the shade of the cliff. Legend has it that the number of flowers blooming is a sign of abundant or scarce water and harvests. People in Anhui deeply believe it and regard it as a sacred object. During the great flood of the 20th year of the Republic (1931), the cliff flower bloomed nine times. This year, the flower bloomed four times, all regarded as a sign of worry-free harvests. The entrance to Xianren Cave is a li from the foot of the cliff, unfathomable. It is said to extend for dozens of li. Although it is just conjecture, its depth can be known. Those traveling with me did not prepare in advance and were pressed for time. They only explored about a li and did not dare to go deeper before returning. Strange rocks grow upside down in the cave, and spring water drips down. A month ago, a Western missionary named Walden from the American Methodist Episcopal Church in Wuhu and his friends went to explore it, carrying grenades and pistols to defend against snakes, beasts, and poisons hidden in the cave. They set off firecrackers as they went, reaching a distance of more than ten li, but the road ahead was still uncertain, and they eventually returned midway. This mysterious cave is gradually attracting the attention of curious people. Someone has initiated the organization of a large-scale expedition to explore it to the fullest.

The Living Stone of Jingtingshan. On the way back, we passed Wang Qiao Cave, located north of Wanjia Mountain, where Prince Qiao is said to have become an immortal. The cave is tall and large, like the city cave of Zhonghua Gate in Nanjing, and dozens of zhang long, passing through the mountain for passage. There are hundreds of stone carvings and statues in the cave, but all have lost their heads, destroyed by superstitious rural farmers. We then passed by Jingtingshan, taking water from Jingtingshan Spring to brew tea on the spot. When tested in a cup, it protruded more than a meter above the cup's rim without spilling, as rumored. Perhaps it contains special minerals. The spring water is clear and pure, and stone crabs can be easily caught. There is also a type of "living stone," which is even more incredible. Upon retrieval and inspection, it is a fine stone that has congealed into the shape of a swallow, about the size of a five-cent coin, with a round hole in the middle. Tiny crawling insects live in the hole. Once the head and fine feet of the insect start to move, the stone is carried along. The name "living stone" is based on this. The greatness of heaven and earth is truly full of wonders. After catching over a hundred of them and placing them in a bottle, we hurried back to Wuhu along the original route. However, it is unknown how long the living stones will live after being transplanted. (May 4th)

Associated Press Interview with Chang Mills on the Reasons for King Haile Selassie's Departure 104

To Reside in Jerusalem as a Private Citizen

According to the China Press, Mr. Mills, a correspondent for the Associated Press who recently left Abyssinia, gave a speech at the American Women's Club yesterday afternoon, stating that in his opinion, there are five reasons for King Haile Selassie's abandonment of Addis Ababa, all of which are purely personal: The King felt that the people would attribute the blame for the defeat to him and might choose someone else as their ruler. The King did not want to suffer the humiliation of being forced to abdicate under Italian rule. The King was truly afraid that his life would be lost at the hands of the Italians. He had several near misses during the war. Mr. Mills said that one day when he was with the King in Taixi, he personally witnessed Italian bombers dropping bombs without warning. The bombs fell very close to the King, but he was unharmed. The King did not flee, but grabbed a machine gun next to him and shot at the enemy plane to defend himself. The King felt that the League of Nations and Britain had plunged Abyssinia into the abyss. The King felt that continuing the war would be difficult to win because the Italian army had tanks, airplanes, poison gas, and other sophisticated new weapons, while the Abyssinian army only had old-fashioned rifles and knives. For these five reasons, he reluctantly fled. Both the King and Queen are devout Christians and now wish to live peacefully in the Holy Land. Mr. Mills believes that the King will enter the Coptic Church and the Queen will enter a convent. He believes that this "King of Kings" could not find a place to live in Abyssinia, so he went to Jerusalem to find it. The situation in Addis Ababa today is chaotic and the overall situation is even more dangerous because ignorant Abyssinians cannot distinguish Italians from other white foreigners. Moreover, the Abyssinians are fanatical and superstitious, and they have a deep hatred for white people. Abyssinian women are very brave, and the courageous actions of the recently deceased American Mrs. Stafford are also admirable. When Italian planes bombed the hospital, Mrs. Stafford completely moved the wounded out of the hospital. Less than three minutes later, the hospital was destroyed by bombs. The King's ancestor lived in Jerusalem. The King and Queen also visited the area several years ago, so they are not strangers when they arrive. The King always carries the Ark of the Covenant when he goes out. The Ark has been by his side during this war. The Abyssinians all believe that the King has survived numerous dangers because of it.

Eurasia Airlines No. 2 Small Aircraft Forced to Land in Ningxia 105

Pilot Yan Duzhou Slightly Injured, Fuselage Slightly Damaged; Passengers Safe, Lanzhou-Baotou Route Still Flying as Usual

According to China Eastern News Agency, the Eurasia Airlines No. 2 small aircraft flying the Lanzhou-Baotou route was forced to land due to weather conditions while approaching Ningxia Station on the 1st of this month. Except for the pilot Yan Duzhou suffering a slight injury to his nose and slight damage to the fuselage, fortunately all four passengers were safe. The Lanzhou-Baotou flight is still flying as usual today. The company is scheduled to send a Junkers Ju 52 large aircraft on the 8th to investigate. China Eastern News Agency reporters specially visited Mr. Zha Zhenhu, the secretary of the company, yesterday morning, and received the following detailed report:

Forced Landing Near Ningxia: The Eurasia Airlines Lanzhou-Baotou route is scheduled to fly one flight every Wednesday and Saturday, returning to Lanzhou and Baotou on the same day. At 8 AM on the 2nd of this month (Saturday), the Lanzhou office of the company dispatched the Eurasia Airlines No. 2 small aircraft as scheduled, piloted by national pilot Yan Duzhou. It took off from Gongxingdun Airfield in Lanzhou. At 9:40 AM, when flying near Ningyuan, the weather suddenly changed, with strong winds and dust, causing the flight to lose direction and had to be forced to land in the area.

Pilot Slightly Injured, Passengers Safe: The location where the aircraft was forced to land was only five kilometers away from the airfield outside the west gate of Ningxia New City. Because the ground was uneven, the aircraft was slightly damaged after landing. The pilot Yan Duzhou was slightly injured in the nose by the impact. Fortunately, all four passengers were safe. After the Ningxia Station office learned of the situation, they immediately sent a car to carry the four passengers and mail into the city. Yan Duzhou was immediately admitted to the hospital for treatment of his injuries.

Lanzhou-Baotou Route Still Flying as Usual Today: The No. 2 small aircraft is currently being repaired by the Ningxia Aircraft Factory. It is expected to be completed within a few days. Because the vibrations caused minor damage, it can still be used after repair and there is no need to claim compensation from the insurance company. Today (Wednesday), the upstream flight on the Lanzhou-Baotou route is still flying from Lanzhou at 8 AM as usual. The company is scheduled to send a Junkers Ju 52 large aircraft from Shanghai to Ningxia on the 8th (Friday) to study the cause of the forced landing.

Yangzhuang Tea Industry Opens Green Tea Drafts Yesterday 106

Chamber of Commerce Chairman Visited Minister Wu Yesterday to Request Relief; Qian Chengxu Telegraphed that He Will Return to Shanghai from Nanjing Today

The Yangzhuang Tea Industry Association, accepting the advice of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, decided to open green tea drafts. However, the loan for Anhui and Jiangxi black tea must wait for a proper resolution before being opened. Samples were sent for trading by various tea firms yesterday morning. The Chairman of the Chamber of Commerce Yu Zuoting visited Minister Wu yesterday to request relief. The details are as follows:

Telegraphic Notice of Opening: The Yangzhuang Tea Industry Association telegraphed to the Chambers of Commerce and Tea Industry Associations in Wuyuan, Tunxi, Shexian, Wenzhou, Changshan, Suian, Weiping, Huzhou, Shaoxing, etc., stating, "This Association has repeatedly received advice from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce and the instructions from the Municipal Government, and will open the market on the 6th, and at the same time, drafts from various places for green tea will be honored. However, due to the unresolved issue with the Transportation and Sales Committee regarding black tea from Anhui and Jiangxi, the drafts will not be honored for the time being. Shanghai Yangzhuang Tea Industry Association humbly submits."

Opening of Trading: The member tea firms of the Yangzhuang Tea Industry Association, including Zhongxin Chang, Hongyuan Yong, Yongxing Long, Zhenhe, Yitai, Yuanfengrun, Gongshengyong, Shenyuan, Rendeyong, Shengchang Sheng, Yilong, Xietai, Tongtai, Xielong, and fourteen others, began honoring all overdue drafts for various green teas yesterday morning, and sent samples of the new green teas from Suian, Shaoxing, Huzhou, and other places that have been listed to various foreign export companies dealing in tea for trading.

Black Tea Issue: The black tea production areas are Qimen and Zhide in Anhui, and Ningzhou, Hekou, Wuning, and Yushan in Jiangxi. The new tea is also about to be listed. Chen Yizhou and others from the Yangzhuang Tea Industry Association are currently negotiating with Cheng Zhenji, Director of the Transportation and Sales Committee, to resolve the Qimen tea transportation and sales issue. Qian Chengxu, a representative sent by the National Chamber of Commerce Federation to petition in Nanjing and Anhui, telegraphed from Nanjing to Shanghai yesterday, reporting that he is scheduled to return to Shanghai today.

Request for Relief: The Chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Yu Zuoting visited Minister of Industry Wu Daquan yesterday to request relief. His original letter is as follows: "To His Excellency Minister Wu Daquan, with utmost respect, the case of the Anhui Provincial Government's control over the transportation and sales of Qimen black tea, which affects the business of tea firms in Shanghai, was reported by the Yangzhuang Tea Industry Association in February and April through telegrams and presented to Your Ministry, requesting consultations with the Anhui Provincial Government to properly address the issue, so as to preserve the decades of overseas trade of the industry. Subsequently, Your Ministry's April telegram stated that an immediate telegram should be sent to urge a prompt resolution and that the control and sales measures should be submitted for review. Although no notification has been received from Your Ministry as to whether the Provincial Government has handled the matter as directed by the telegram, in reality, the situation is becoming increasingly pressing, making the tea firms feel that there is no business to conduct. For example, tea firms used to lend money to tea producers as their business. When the Provincial Government decided to control Qimen black tea, its decision document stated that the unemployment and debts of export tea merchants (i.e., tea firms) must be taken into account. The Anhui Provincial Government's reply to the Chamber of Commerce in its winter telegram in March stated that measures were being carefully studied and would not hinder the lending of tea firms, and requested that this be communicated to dispel any doubts. Its expression of not competing with the people for profit was particularly earnest. However, while claiming to be carefully studying the matter, it established the Transportation and Sales Committee in Anhui Province on April 1. Moreover, tea producers who had already received loans from tea firms but did not want to receive official loans were also forced to comply. The Anhui Provincial Black Tea Transportation and Sales Committee's April telegram claiming that more than 1.9 million yuan had been loaned was an implicit indication of its efforts to take over the lending business. Tea firms feel disappointed that the Anhui Provincial Government's words and actions contradict each other, and that it first comforted them and then reversed its decision. However, in order to preserve the commercial market, they sent representatives to Anhui Provincial Government to propose a government-transported, merchant-sold approach. According to the tea firms' report, this approach was verbally approved. However, the Anhui Provincial Government's April telegram differed from the verbally approved approach. Only a sales group was established under the Transportation and Sales Committee's General Sales Office to recruit tea firm personnel to handle the business. The main body of transportation and sales remained with the province, and tea firms were merely employees. Thus, the tea firms' lending and transportation business was entirely taken over by the province. The province's so-called control is actually a euphemism for state-owned operation. Unable to bear this any longer, the tea firms stopped honoring all types of notes issued previously that were due for payment on April 23. The reason for this action was that the current loan was originally granted with the special permission of Anhui Province, stating that it would "not hinder" the tea firms. Now that the province has gone back on its word, the responsibility should be borne by the province itself, and since the tea firms are on the verge of forced closure, they are in fact unable to bear this burden. For half a month, the various tea-producing counties in the interior, which relied on these notes for circulation, have felt a sense of financial stagnation once the notes were stopped from being honored. Moreover, because of the impact of the closure of tea firms, green tea exports have also been affected at the same time. Therefore, Anhui's current measures are not only related to the survival of the Shanghai tea firms, but also to the rise and fall of the national tea export industry. If Anhui Province relies on its abundant public power and does not leave any room for tea firms, it is feared that the officials and merchants will become the snipe and clam, while others may become the fisherman, leading to the complete destruction of the only remaining tea export industry in the so-called Qimen black tea control policy. Today, the concept of economic control and industrial control is prevalent. The so-called control is not intended to exclude private enterprises and replace them with state-owned enterprises. The province's claim to control Qimen black tea, while ending up with government transportation and sales, is inevitably leading down the wrong path. Moreover, it is causing people to misunderstand the meaning of the concept, claiming that the various types of control advocated by current trends are the prelude to nationalizing all industries, especially fearing that the false claims will spread, causing great anxiety in the business community and further shrinking investment. This is what I repeatedly considered and dared not fail to directly report to Your Excellency. I, Zuoting, humbly serve as the chairman of the Chamber of Commerce, and it is my duty to do so. I have earnestly advised the industry to open its market and resume operations in order to avoid a chain reaction in this spring's tea market. At the same time, the Chamber of Commerce sent telegrams to the National Economic Commission and the Municipal Government, requesting them to consult with Anhui Province to adopt the compromise measure of government transportation and merchant sales proposed by the industry, so that tea merchants' businesses can be preserved. All avenues for appeal have been exhausted, but no results have been seen, causing me to feel ashamed and fearful. Having no other choice, I respectfully submit this letter to Your Excellency, earnestly requesting Your Excellency to exert all your influence to help, and to consult with Anhui Province to adopt the original compromise proposal of the industry immediately to properly resolve the issue, which is in the public interest. With utmost respect, I wish you good health."

Agricultural Loan Consortium Begins Handling Loans 107

Telegraphed to Hebei, Shaanxi, and Anhui Three Regions Yesterday to Begin Handling Immediately; Targeting Cotton and Agricultural Warehouses

The China Agricultural Cooperative Loan Consortium, after the board of directors meeting decided on a loan amount of 2.5 million yuan for this year and stipulated that the loan areas would be Hebei, Shaanxi, and Anhui provinces, specializing in cotton and agricultural warehouses, telegraphed to the Anhui Bank of Communications, Shaanxi Shanghai Bank, and Hebei Jincheng Bank offices in the three regions yesterday after the loan was released, instructing them to begin accepting loans immediately to help farmers develop agriculture.

海州將子港外　兩裝鹽輪擱淺 108

Fengpu and Qingning Both Telegraphed Shanghai Reports Yesterday

The Sanbei Company's Fengpu steamer, with a loading capacity of 1,911 tons and 800 horsepower, capable of traveling ten nautical miles per hour, was originally sailing the Yangtze River. It was dispatched this time to Shierxu to load a large quantity of Huai salt for unloading within the Yangtze River. Yesterday afternoon at 5:30, the steamer departed from Haizhou fully loaded with Huai salt. Unexpectedly, when it sailed to

Jiangzi Port, about thirty-five li from Haizhou, the steamer, due to its heavy load and shallow water, ran aground suddenly outside Jiangzi Port. The hull became stuck in the port shoal. The shipowner, Chang Sheng, attempted to free the ship himself, repeatedly reversing the engine, but to no avail. The water at the grounding site was only sixteen feet deep at most, leaving the shipowner with no recourse. He telegraphed Shanghai yesterday morning,

reporting the grounding situation and requesting advice on waiting for the tide and rescue measures. The company received the report in the afternoon and telegraphed instructions to wait for the rising tide and try to get the ship off the shoal. If the grounding was too severe and self-rescue was impossible, the cargo should be unloaded to reduce the draft. Therefore, they are currently waiting for further telegrams. Furthermore, according to continuous reports, at the same time as the Fengpu steamer encountered grounding outside Jiangzi Port, there was also the

Qingning Steamer, also fully loaded with Huai salt destined for the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. It had set sail several hours before the Fengpu steamer. Upon sailing to the outside of Jiangzi Port, it also ran aground, with the hull stuck in the shoal. The situation was also quite serious. Yesterday afternoon, Shanghai also received a telegram about this. Currently, it is waiting for the tide for rescue along with the Fengpu steamer.

南翔站　查獲漏稅外絲 109

Nanyang Station Seized Smuggled Foreign Silk

Suzhou Also Seized More Than Ten Thousand Yuan Worth of Foreign Silk

The Nanxiang station discovered four large rattan boxes a few days ago with no one claiming them. The stationmaster, Lu Jiafu, along with the railway police, opened them for inspection and found that they all contained smuggled foreign silk, totaling forty bundles worth seven hundred and twenty yuan. The items were escorted to Shanghai. Yesterday, a report was made to Mr. Balunsen, the Customs Commissioner of the Jianghai Customs, who dispatched personnel to retrieve the goods for confiscation by the Customs. It is reported that on the same day, the Suzhou station also seized thirty large boxes of artificial silk, worth over ten thousand yuan, according to reports.

復旦大學各級同學　昨日完全上課 110

All Levels of Students at Fudan University Fully Resumed Classes Yesterday

Seven Students Disciplined and the Matter Concluded

According to the Huadong News Agency, the students of Fudan University in Jiangwan went on strike to support the seven students who had been arrested. This led the school authorities to expel the seven students in the support association, causing a misunderstanding that classes were suspended. Subsequently, after repeated requests from the students to President Li Denghui, the expulsion was changed to two major demerits. All students returned to school as usual starting on the 4th. The 5th was a holiday for a memorial day. Starting today, all levels of students have fully resumed classes, and the order has returned to normal.

Page 11

市公安局努力禁烟　破獲烟窟三百餘處　烟民總檢舉定五月十日開始　公務人員限兩個月自新戒除 115

The Municipal Public Security Bureau Strives to Ban Smoking and Destroys Over 300 Opium Dens; General Reporting of Smokers Scheduled to Begin on May 10; Government Employees Given Two Months to Reform and Quit

The general reporting of smokers in this city is scheduled to begin on the 10th of this month. The Municipal Public Security Bureau is actively striving to eliminate opium addiction within the district and has destroyed over 300 opium dens in recent days. Government employees of party, government, and military agencies are given a two-month deadline to quit. Details are as follows:

Gradually Eliminating Opium Dens

The Municipal Public Security Bureau considers the secret private opium dens throughout the city, which supply opium for smoking, to be the source of opium addicts, and even a place where bandits are harbored. Therefore, the Bureau ordered all district offices to make efforts over several months, resulting in the destruction of opium dens and the dismantling of organizations that sell red pills, morphine, and other drugs in various districts such as Nanshi, Pudong, Zhabei, Jiangwan, Wusong, Fahua, Pusong, Pengpu, Gaoqiao, Longhua, etc., totaling over 350 locations (excluding those with gun licenses). To completely eliminate all secret private opium dens, the Public Security Bureau encourages people to report them and, in addition to keeping the identity of the informants confidential, provides appropriate rewards. If it is discovered that any government officials are protecting the situation, they will be severely punished.

Enthusiastic Supplementary Registration

Since the Military Affairs Commission issued instructions to the responsible anti-drug agencies to allow smokers to register supplementally to give them a final chance to reform, and the Songhu Garrison Command handed over convicted and unconvicted opium offenders to the Public Security Bureau after a written pledge and allowed them to register supplementally, all the smokers in the city have been applying to the Smoker Registration Section of the Fourth Division of the Public Security Bureau and the district offices in recent days, because the general reporting work is about to begin. The number of applicants exceeds 2,000. No fees or fines are charged. As for the second phase of license renewal for registered smokers, the number has also exceeded six-tenths of the total registration number.

Reporting of Government Employees

The general reporting of smokers throughout the city is scheduled to begin on the 10th of this month. Various implementation plans for reporting smokers will be announced in the coming days. As for government employees of party, government, and military agencies, they will be strictly reported as a model for the people in order to enforce the anti-drug policy. The reporting methods are as follows: The reporting period is set for two months. During the first month, each employee must submit a written pledge stating that they do not smoke opium or use drugs, which must be stamped and certified by their direct superior. During the second month, the competent authorities will compile and forward the pledges to the General Reporting Agency. After the pledge, if it is discovered or reported and verified that they are drug users, they will be dismissed from their original positions or sent for punishment.

我國僑務問題　周啟剛廣播演講 116

Zhou Qigang Gives Radio Speech on Overseas Chinese Affairs

Central Committee Member Zhou Qigang was recently invited by the Ministry of Education to be a lecturer on public education at the Ministry. He delivered speeches on the Central Radio Station on April 29th and May 2nd, titled "The Problem of Our Overseas Chinese Affairs." The original manuscript is published below:

Today, at the invitation of Minister Wang of the Ministry of Education, I am here to broadcast on the scheduled topic, "The Problem of Our Overseas Chinese Affairs." This problem has a very broad meaning, and I have published several parts of it over the years. Now, I will combine the old concepts and new thoughts and divide them into four sections: 1. The Definition of Overseas Chinese Affairs; 2. The Chinese People's Understanding of the Issue of Emigration; 3. The Form of Overseas Chinese Administration; 4. The Key to the Survival of Overseas Chinese, and present them to everyone.

The Definition of Overseas Chinese Affairs

The issue of Overseas Chinese affairs has already become a central issue in the world's evolution for hundreds of years in the international arena. Just look at the various countries' efforts to strengthen their military, develop shipping lanes, increase tonnage, expand territory, seize markets, extract raw materials, and even so-called island trusteeships and mandated territories, etc. All the open and covert struggles are derived from this issue. However, in the past, our country's history has either been self-righteous or self-destructive about the issue of Overseas Chinese affairs, mostly believing that there is nothing outside of China, and that everyone except the Chinese are barbarians. General political and economic issues have long been ignored, so when discussing the issue of Overseas Chinese affairs today, we must first analyze the definition of Overseas Chinese affairs. The term "Overseas Chinese Affairs," in its general sense, refers to the administrative affairs that a country handles regarding the emigration of its own people to foreign countries and the immigration of foreign people into its own country. However, the management of emigration differs in each country in the world. Some countries do not focus on managing the emigration of their own people, but on managing their colonies. Some manage the emigration of their own people while expanding their territories. Some have no territories at all and only manage their own immigrants. Our country's Overseas Chinese affairs, of course, belong to the latter. Because of our country's national strength and various other reasons, although many foreigners have immigrated to China, we have not implemented appropriate management. Article 1 of our current Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission's organizational law states: "...manages the emigration and protection of its own people," which is also particularly different from others. In various countries, so-called emigration either involves having a colony before having colonial actions, or a country having an immigration policy before having immigration management. However, our emigration and management are not like this. It is because there has long been the fact of "people's emigration" that Overseas Chinese organizations have been established recently. This is especially special. Therefore, we can only talk about managing our own Overseas Chinese at present, so our scope of Overseas Chinese affairs is biased in terms of the definition of Overseas Chinese affairs.

The Chinese People's Understanding of the Issue of Emigration

I said earlier that the most important evolution over the past hundreds of years in the world is the issue of international emigration. Let us think, as far back as the invasion of Europe by the Goths and Vandals, the migration of Huns and other Asians into Europe, the expansion of Turks from Asia to Asia Minor, the colonization of England by the Normans, the wars of the Romans and Alexander, the long march of Greeks along the Mediterranean coast, the exploration of the New World by Europeans across the Atlantic, the scramble for islands in the Pacific and Indian Oceans by France, Italy, Portugal, Spain, Britain, Japan, and the occupation of coastal islands and borderlands of our country, and as recent as the Eastern Philippine War, the turbulence of the international situation is a strong expression of the colonial issue. So-called international events and world issues are all concentrated on the solution of colonialism. This is something that everyone can see. Looking back at our country's past history, not only was emigration not taken care of, but even in the Manchu Qing Dynasty, harsh punishments were used to absolutely prohibit citizens from moving abroad. At the same time, the general public also held a contemptuous attitude towards seeking a livelihood abroad. How strange is this? However, although our government and people have had such disregard for the issue of emigration in the past, the number of emigrants from our Overseas Chinese exceeds the number of emigrants from all other countries in the world, and the spread of Overseas Chinese businesses has also achieved considerable success. This is indeed a characteristic of our country's commerce. Regarding this point, I have also published the reasons for its existence, which I will not repeat here. However, what we should pay attention to is that modern countries and modern nations must not ignore the issue of emigration if they want to maintain their survival, because a country and a nation cannot close themselves off in the midst of turbulent world trends, let alone seek a way out in the international arena in order to achieve a balance between people and resources. Therefore, we should recognize the Overseas Chinese issue that arises from emigration is an important policy that every country should use to deal with people and resources in the international arena. The past attitudes of self-righteousness and self-abandonment should be thoroughly reformed. Originally, the emigration of Overseas Chinese also occupies an important position in international politics and economics, which has been recognized by historical facts. The most serious and difficult problem in the world is the unemployment problem of surplus labor. From a general international political and economic point of view, the issues of emigration and unemployment are mutually related. This close relationship is naturally formed because the outward movement of the people of one country can reduce domestic unemployment and increase foreign financial resources, so countries are fighting for the goal of "colonies and colonization." The issue of emigration has become an important focus of international politics and economics, but the overseas emigration of our compatriots and the colonizers who are fighting for colonies are completely different, because in international politics and economics, we not only have no danger of fighting, but also make peaceful and great contributions to the place of emigration. This important meaning of the emigration of Overseas Chinese should be paid special attention to and should be explained: the progress and prosperity of various businesses in the world are all based on labor. Before the nineteenth century, North America, such as the United States and Canada, South America, such as Chile, Brazil, and Mexico, and the rest, such as Australia and the South Seas Islands, were all barren lands that were left unmanaged. None of today's prosperity was achieved without using the labor of Overseas Chinese. Our compatriots have low wages, are hard-working, and can work tirelessly for the place of residence year after year, regardless of whether they are the hosts or the guests. This is the first meaning of Overseas Chinese emigration expressed internationally. Overseas Chinese not only contribute labor to the place of residence, but also export and digest our inherent great culture to the people of the place of residence. According to what I have observed in the overseas Chinese residence areas, especially the local culture in various places in the South Seas Islands, all contain important elements of Chinese culture, and the same Western culture, in its initial stage or even now, is directly or indirectly influenced by Chinese culture, at least making Chinese and Western cultures communicate and harmonize with each other. This is the second meaning of Overseas Chinese emigration expressed internationally. In the early stages of development of various countries and colonies, there is a feeling of too little population. Increasing the population is a natural requirement. Overseas emigration of Overseas Chinese provides for their needs, enriches their labor force, and promotes their development. Internationally, it regulates the density of the population and the equilibrium of labor supply and demand. This is the third meaning of Overseas Chinese emigration expressed internationally. From these three meanings, the emigration of our Overseas Chinese is beneficial to our country and nation, and it is also beneficial to the people of the world. Unfortunately, in the past, our country ignored the issue of emigration too much, so although there are so many people emigrating abroad, there is still no proper management and policy, and the general public in society also lacks a deep understanding of this emigration undertaking, which "exports labor to reduce the difficulty of social labor and sends capital internally to increase the economic lifeline of the country." Originally, a nation should have a spirit of courage and enterprise in order to stand on its own in the world. If it is still holding on to a state of shrinking, peace, fear, and depression, then there is absolutely no spirit of outward expansion. No wonder our territory and sovereignty are being taken away day by day. Look at how Japan values this issue of emigration. There is no need to talk about the various efforts of its government. Just look at the societies organized by them and the publications exploring the issue of emigration in their society. There are so many. We are really dwarfed by them. Our country's past isolation from the issue of emigration certainly has political and historical reasons, but the social atmosphere also has a lot of influence. For example, life is considered difficult and humble when one leaves one's hometown, unfilial when one travels far from home, and disrespectful when one lives with barbarians for a long time... These are all obstacles to understanding the issue of emigration. In recent years, we have temporarily changed under the pressure of external forces. I hope that everyone will have a deep understanding of the issue of emigration from now on, and strive with peace and courage to enable the country and nation to achieve the happiness of coexistence and common prosperity in the world. This is the meaning of recognizing the issue of emigration. (To be continued)

非觀光團領袖萬氏　昨晨拜會吳市長　吳市長市商會均將歡宴 119

Mr. Wan, Leader of a Non-Tourist Group, Visited Mayor Wu Yesterday Morning; Mayor Wu and the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Will Host a Banquet

Mr. Manwcl A. Alzatc, a member of the Philippine Congress, a journalist, and the head of the Sino-Japanese Tourist Group, led the group. Except for the journalist part, there are still five people in Japan who will come to China later. Mr. Wan and his group of six arrived in Shanghai on the President Coolidge ship of the Da Lai Company the day before yesterday. Only Mr. Wan stayed in China as a representative. The other five, including Wei Lai Niuwa, left Shanghai on the same ship at 8 o'clock yesterday morning and returned to the Philippines via Hong Kong. After arriving in Shanghai, Mr. Wan stayed at the New Asia Hotel. At 11:30 yesterday morning, he took the letter of introduction from Mr. Li Haoju, Consul General of our country in Manila, and was accompanied by Zhang Nanin, a representative from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, to visit Mayor Wu at the Municipal Government to express his respect. The Mayor received him with Secretary Tang Shixuan, exchanged greetings, and chatted for about half an hour before leaving. The Mayor will host a banquet in the next few days to show the hospitality of the host. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce plans to hold a banquet after a part of the journalist members of the delegation arrive in Shanghai in order to connect their feelings. Mr. Wan is scheduled to go to Beijing in two or three days to pay respects to Foreign Minister Zhang and other central authorities, and to visit scenic spots in Suzhou and Hangzhou, and then return to Shanghai to wait for a boat to return to the Philippines after about one week.

The Spring Cocoon Syndicate Started Lending Simultaneously in Shanghai, Hangzhou, and Wuxi Yesterday; Spring Cocoons in Various Places in Jiangsu and Zhejiang Are About to Be on the Market; Various Factories are Repairing Machinery and Preparing to Start Production

After the establishment of the Spring Cocoon Lending Syndicate of Jiangsu and Zhejiang in 1925, the Shanghai General Office and the Hangzhou and Wuxi Branch Offices started lending for cocoon harvesting simultaneously yesterday. Spring cocoons in Jiangsu and Zhejiang are about to be on the market. Details are as follows:

Lending for Cocoon Harvesting Started Yesterday

The Shanghai General Office of the Syndicate (inside the General Office of the Bank of Communications), and the Hangzhou and Wuxi branch offices (inside the Hangzhou and Wuxi branches of the Bank of China) started processing cocoon harvesting and lending yesterday. All manufacturers in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces who wish to borrow for cocoon harvesting can apply to the General and Branch Offices of the Syndicate, and must provide at least 30% down payment and a reliable guarantor in accordance with the Syndicate's regulations. The loan period is three months, the interest rate is 8.5%, and the application deadline is May 20 in Zhejiang and May 25 in Jiangsu. The committee organized by the Syndicate will review and approve the loans at any time.

Spring Cocoons in Jiangsu and Zhejiang Are About to Be on the Market

This year's spring cocoons in Jiangsu and Zhejiang: Cocoon markets in Shaoxing, Haining, and other places in Zhejiang are scheduled to open on May 18, and cocoon markets in Jiaxing, Pinghu, and other places are scheduled to open on May 20. Cocoon markets in Wuxi, Liyang, and other places in Jiangsu are scheduled to open around May 25. Silk manufacturers and silkworm cocoon merchants have been very busy organizing cocoon collection agencies to prepare to start collecting cocoons in the past few days. This cocoon collection is divided into improved varieties and local varieties, but the output of spring cocoons in various places, the improved varieties account for seventy to eighty percent.

Various Silk Factories Prepare to Start Production

Since the banks and money shops jointly formed the Spring Cocoon Lending Syndicate and stipulated the lending methods, the banks and money shops that have not joined the lending methods will also follow the syndicate's methods. Silk manufacturers in Shanghai, Wuxi, and Hangzhou are preparing to start silk reeling after collecting the spring cocoons. The silk factories that have been shut down are repairing machinery and preparing everything. The current price of Chinese silk in foreign countries, the B-grade is about 700 yuan in Chinese currency, which is about the same as before.

Bureau of Social Affairs to Conduct Boiler Inspections 122

The Factory Inspection Division of the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, in view of the extreme negligence of various factories in the city regarding boiler facilities, such as whether the boiler body is capable of withstanding the normal operating pressure, whether scale has accumulated inside the boiler, whether there are leaks in the boiler plates, and whether all gauges are accurate, lacks thorough inspections. Even when inspections are carried out, they are performed by mechanics lacking experience, so boiler explosions occur from time to time, which not only harms workers and factories but also disrupts the tranquility of the entire society. Therefore, when starting the second phase of factory inspection work, the division plans to first implement boiler inspections to reduce disasters and protect the safety of factories, workers, and the tranquility of the entire society. It is reported that the division will implement inspections in phases in accordance with the Factory Safety and Health Inspection Regulations promulgated by the Ministry of Industry, in order to ensure that all equipment in factories in the city meets safety and health standards. Regarding boiler inspection matters, drafting of inspection methods has now begun, and it is expected to start implementation in early next month.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Resumes Northern Route with "Xinming" Vessel; Southern "Nanhua" Schedule Remains Unchanged 126

The Southern "Nanhua" line of the state-owned China Merchants Steam Navigation Company originally consisted of the Yuanheng, Lizhen, four new seagoing vessels, and the Anxing vessel, five ships in total, departing from Shanghai to Guangzhou every Sunday and Wednesday. However, the Bureau found that departing on Sundays was inconvenient for guest customs declarations, and the frequent trips of the vessels meant that the time spent docked in Shanghai was very short, and the inspection work was also rushed. Therefore, for the convenience of guests and inspection work, starting from May 1st, the departure schedule was changed to every Wednesday, Thursday, and Saturday, departing from Shanghai. The Gongping vessel was also assigned to join the schedule, so that each vessel could spend an extra day docked in Shanghai for inspection. Therefore, the actual number of trips was not reduced. As for the "Xinming" vessel, which was originally a Northern route vessel of the Bureau, it had previously been rerouted to Fuzhou due to the Tianjin ice floes. Now that the Tianjin Haihe River has returned to its original state, the "Xinming" vessel has resumed the Northern route as before. The Shanghai-Fuzhou route has been taken over by the Yushun vessel, and the Shanghai-Fuzhou route has not been suspended.

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce is continuing to handle the registration of creditors in the Wing On Silver Company composition case, and has convened another meeting of creditors. The announcement states that the Chamber has accepted the Wing On Silver Company's request for a composition in accordance with the Bankruptcy Law. However, because the number of creditors attending on that day was insufficient to meet the legal quorum, it was decided to postpone it to May 23rd, Saturday, at 2:00 PM for a re-convening. Starting from today, the registration of creditors will continue. All unregistered creditors are requested to bring their creditor certificates to the Chamber for verification and registration before May 22nd, and to obtain a registration certificate and voting ticket so that they can attend the meeting on time to discuss matters. Any delay is of utmost importance. This announcement.

Continued Trial of Assassination of Japanese Sailor; Mysterious and Unpredictable Content 131

Ye Haisheng Admits Everything and is Willing to Accept National Law; Zhang Chen Proves that Ye Haisheng was Framed

Yang Wendao and Ye Haisheng (nickname "Little Guangdong"), Guangdong natives accused of shooting and killing Japanese sailor Nakayama Hideo on Baole An Road at 9:00 PM on November 9th last year, have already been publicly tried once by the First Special District Court. This was reported in previous newspapers. At 2:00 PM yesterday, Chief Judge Qian Hongye of the Criminal Division, together with Assessors Feng Shide and Xiao Xiefei, formed a collegial panel in the First Court to continue the hearing. Prosecutor Zhang Zongru also attended to perform his duties. Municipal Government Secretary Zhang Tingrong and Section Chief Huang Hua of the Municipal Public Security Bureau's Third Section also attended to observe. The Japanese Naval Headquarters in Shanghai also sent several officers and soldiers to listen. In addition, there were no fewer than a hundred onlookers. The police station lawyer Ru Bao Yi first reported the names of the people who had been summoned to testify, and then said that the defendant Ye Haisheng had written a statement in the police station after the previous trial, which was more detailed than his previous confession in court. According to him, he and Yang Wendao met when Yang was the chairman of the Chongshun Mutual Aid Society. Later, Yang successively organized the Tongyi Coordination Association and the Tongren Coordination Association, with Yang as the chairman and him as a member. The killing of the Japanese soldier was discussed twice in the Tongyi Coordination Association in early and late October. In addition to him and Yang, those who attended the meeting included Zhou Shiyong, the Korean Han Jieke, and another Korean whose name he did not know. On November 2nd, the five of them went out together to choose a location that would be convenient for committing the crime, in order to make it easier to escape after the crime, etc. He also presented a large drawing of the location where the incident occurred, as well as a page of drawings of the pistol bullets found by the detective at the scene after the incident, along with the various exhibits that had been presented previously. Next, two Chinese policemen, No. 2891 and No. 2864, reported the situation of finding Nakayama Hideo injured and lying on the ground, saying that at 9:03 PM on November 9th, while patrolling near the Japanese headquarters on North Sichuan Road, they were informed by passers-by Hu Xianghe and a 13- or 14-year-old girl that someone was lying in a pool of blood. They went to check and immediately telegraphed the police station. The court then summoned witness Hu Xianghe, who testified that he was a shoemaker. That night, he went to the Japanese shoemaker Takaoka's shop at No. 90 Baole An Road to collect debts. When he arrived at the entrance of the lane, he saw two rickshaws and a car parked there, and then heard a gunshot. He saw a person fleeing from the Fengle Lane, wearing black clothes and trousers. He did not notice whether the person was wearing a hat. He immediately entered Takaoka's shop to tell Takaoka, and then went out together to check, and found that the person lying on the ground was a Japanese sailor. He then went to the police station with the two Chinese policemen to report everything. The Japanese Takaoka then testified that he was playing a record player in the shop at the time, when he suddenly heard an explosion, and then Hu arrived and told him what happened, so he went out together to check the situation. The Japanese Navy Marine Corps medical officer He Jia Hui (transliteration) testified that he examined Nakayama Hideo's body. The bullet entered from the back of the head and exited from the forehead. The wound and the recovered bullet were very consistent. (These two witnesses gave their statements in Japanese, so they had to be translated into English first, and then translated into Chinese by the translator Jiang Baoliang.) The court then summoned witness Yao Afu, the wife of Zeng Yuanzhi, who testified that she lived at No. 6 Fengle Lane, North Sichuan Road. She did not know Ye Haisheng at first, but only saw him when he came to her husband with a pistol to pawn it for 25 yuan, but the money was not borrowed. The loan application he wrote was torn up because of this case. At first, I thought that my husband's friend Zheng Weimin had reported it to the police station, but I later learned that it was Zhang Chen, because Zhang originally lived in my house. When my husband talked to Zheng about this matter, he could hear it. Chief Judge Qian then questioned the defendant Ye Haisheng. Unexpectedly, Ye not only wanted to overturn his previous confession in court, but also denied his recent statement written in the police station, saying that the words in the statement were fabricated by him, so if he were to repeat them, he would have forgotten most of them. In short, Nakayama Hideo was killed by him alone, and he was willing to state the process in court. He had been planning it for a long time, and because he encountered the sailor that night, he shot him. The books that were found were his, and the holes in the books were also dug by him. The court found his testimony strange, so he asked him, "The books belong to Yang Wendao, and the holes in the books were also dug by Yang. Now you claim that they are yours. On this point alone, it is clear that your testimony is difficult to believe. And you previously confessed in the police station that two Koreans wanted to hit the sailor, so why are you now admitting to the crime?" Ye then confessed that he was still confused when he wrote the confession in the police station, but now he feels that since this matter was done by me, I cannot falsely accuse others. Yang Wendao did not go with me either. The reason why I falsely accused others last time was because I hoped that I would not be severely punished and that I could still do something after I was released from prison. Now I am willing to accept the national law. That night, I was wearing black clothes and not wearing a hat, etc. When questioned, Yang Wendao still denied it, and said that the Tongren Association never had foreign members, and never invited Zhou Shiyong to the association to discuss any matters. The court then summoned Hu Xianghe and ordered him to identify whether there was anyone he saw fleeing that night among the two defendants. Hu repeatedly shook his head, indicating that he could not identify them, but Ye immediately said that although Hu did not see me that night, I did see Hu. At this time, the lawyer for the defendant Yang Wendao made some arguments, while the police station lawyer Ru Bao Yi requested to continue questioning the witnesses, and stated that Zhang Chen suddenly surrendered to the police station yesterday afternoon, saying that he knew the details of the case, and then took out a draft of a book and read it aloud. After he finished speaking, he presented the draft to the court. Then, Ye Atao, a tea servant from the Tongren Association, testified that Yang Wendao came to the association every day from one or two in the afternoon until midnight, without interruption. Ye Haisheng occasionally went to the association once or twice a month. There were more than 500 members in the association, none of whom were foreigners. At this time, Yang's lawyer had brought Zhang Chen to the court. Chief Judge Qian questioned him and learned that he was from Yaoyao County, Guangdong, and currently lived at No. 8 Chuan Gong Road. He did not know Yang. Because I knew the details of the case, I asked a friend surnamed Ye to write a report, which I originally planned to submit to the court. I had been friends with Zeng Yuan since childhood. After returning to Shanghai from Fujian in August last year, I often went to Zeng's house to chat until the end of the lunar year. A friend wanted to mortgage his property, so I went to visit him on December 10th to ask if he had any clients. Zheng Weimin was also at Zeng's house that day, and I saw them smoking and drawing a pistol on paper with a pencil. On December 29th, Zeng invited me to go to Zheng's house with him, saying that he was going to get money, but because he did not meet him, Zeng was quite upset. At that time, Zeng said that Zheng had asked him to go to the house of a Japanese officer to identify the pistol that killed the Japanese sailor, promising to pay him. Now Zheng is avoiding him and not paying him, which is hateful. But after Zeng returned, Zheng came immediately, so Zeng introduced us to each other. From then on, Zeng and Zheng talked without avoiding me at all. On January 4th, my brother sent a letter from Sichuan. Zheng took the envelope because he needed it. The next day, Zheng came to me and said, "There is a matter now. If you are willing to do it, you can get a reward of 4,000 yuan." I asked what it was. Zheng said that if he could report to the Japanese military headquarters that Nakayama Hideo was shot and killed by Ye Haisheng, Yang Wendao, and the Korean Han Jieke, he could get this huge reward. Zheng also said that Jieke had been captured by the Japanese, and he was willing to take me to identify him. Because I knew Ye well, I could not bear to do this, so I replied that I would consider it. Two days later, Zheng came to talk again, and asked me to go to the Japanese consulate to identify Jieke. On the way, I finally realized that it was dangerous, and returned alone and told Zeng about it. I also asked Zeng to return the envelope to Zheng. A few days later, I heard Zheng and Zeng say that they would think of another way. So they found Zhang Caiyuan (that is, the witness Zhang Kaiyuan mentioned in the previous report) and told him what they had told me, ordering Zhang to report to the Japanese military headquarters, etc. The court then asked Zeng whether Zhang Chen's statement was true. Zeng first said that Zhang's statement was all what he told him, and then suddenly attacked him, saying that Zhang originally lived in his house, but unexpectedly took advantage of his trip to Qingdao to go to a hotel room with his wife (that is, Yao Afu). He is a shameless and unscrupulous person, which immediately aroused the interest of the onlookers, who all smiled. Then Zhang Caiyuan was summoned for questioning, who said that Zhang Chen really wanted to get the reward and repeatedly came to talk to me, asking me to report to the police station as soon as possible. Because I had not seen the murderer, I hesitated, etc. The police station lawyer then requested to release Zhang Chen on bail. Chief Judge Qian, believing that there was no need to order bail, ordered that the hearing be continued on May 20th, and Yang and Ye were returned to custody.

Cut into Two Sections, Viscera Exposed; Autopsy and Coffin Preparation Yesterday, Seeking Claimants

At approximately 10:00 PM on the 5th, in front of the Chuan Gong Road intersection of the Songhu branch line, when the 150th Songhu local train was passing through the area, a man of approximately 30 years old, wearing a short blue cloth shirt and pants, and resembling a worker, suddenly ran onto the tracks, causing him to be cut in half at the waist by the train, with his viscera exposed, blood and flesh in a mess, and a tragic death on the tracks.
