Popular Lectures

The Righteous Man Wang 205

— Su Zihan

After the Qing dynasty destroyed the Ming dynasty, it issued an order requiring all people in Jiangnan to shave their hair and wear it in a queue. At that time, the Qing dynasty had just seized power and its power was immense. This order was carried out with great force. Who would dare to disobey? Only those with the heart of a tiger and the gall of a leopard, not afraid of losing their heads.

When the order reached Rugao County in Taizhou, the people of Rugao County all obeyed the order, shaved their hair, and wore it in a queue. Only one person, named Xu Yuanbo, refused. Xu Yuanbo was neither an official nor a scholar, but just an ordinary commoner.

Xu Yuanbo said very well, "I am Chinese. Why should I listen to the foreign emperor's words and shave my hair? The foreign emperor killed our emperor and occupied our land. Is that not enough? He still wants to control our hair. If I shave my hair, wouldn't I become a slave of the foreign emperor? I can't do it! You can kill my head, but I cannot shave my hair!"

These words reached the ears of the government officials, and they were all shocked. They all thought, "This is terrible! Defying the imperial decree! If we don't deal with him, our superiors will know, and it may harm our future!" So they sent people to arrest Xu Yuanbo's family and question him. Xu Yuanbo directly admitted it without denying anything. They reported the details to their superiors and sentenced Xu Yuanbo to death for defying the imperial decree. He was taken to the execution ground and beheaded. Xu Yuanbo's wife was also sentenced to exile and was about to set off immediately.

At that time, there was a yamen runner in Rugao County named Wang. There were not many kind people among the yamen runners. Although Runner Wang was a yamen runner, he had a few hard bones in his body, was loyal, righteous, and valued friendship. He usually did many things to help people in the yamen, which fit the saying "It is good to practice virtue in the yamen." His colleagues all respected him, and the people in the county who knew him also respected him. They did not call him by his name, but called him the Righteous Man Wang.

Xu Yuanbo refused to shave his hair and was beheaded. He died loyally and righteously. Those who knew him all sighed and shed a few tears. Xu Yuanbo's death was not enough. His wife was also exiled, which made people feel even more pity and anger.

When Xu Yuanbo was imprisoned and had not yet been beheaded, the Righteous Man Wang wanted to save him. But he was just a yamen runner, and it could not even be said that he was "a low-ranking official with a small position." What ability did he have to save Xu Yuanbo? He could only watch helplessly as the executioner took Xu Yuanbo's head from his neck and watched helplessly as Xu Yuanbo's wife was exiled! Alas! The escort was also assigned to the Righteous Man Wang.

The Righteous Man Wang received the document from the county magistrate and walked onto the street, thinking to himself, "It's good that I was assigned, so that Mistress Xu won't suffer on the road. Alas! Such a loyal and righteous person as Xu Yuanbo was killed by these muddleheaded fools. Killing him was not enough, they also had to exile Mistress Xu! Alas! I wanted to save Xu Yuanbo before, but I had no way to save him. Now that I am escorting Mistress Xu, I must find a way to save her."

The Righteous Man Wang walked and thought, and before he knew it, he had reached his own home.

Until late at night, the Righteous Man Wang had not yet thought of a way to save Mistress Xu. Originally, this was not an easy task. He was the escort and could not casually release the prisoner. There was only one way: to find another woman to impersonate Mistress Xu so that Mistress Xu could be released. This was a good method. But where to find such a person? Who would be willing to give up their comfortable life and go to suffer for others? This was truly the most difficult thing in the world.

This matter troubled the Righteous Man Wang. He did not sleep well all night, but tossed and turned in bed, sighing. The Righteous Man Wang was usually not like this, but today he suddenly acted this way. Madam Wang could not help but be surprised, so she asked, "Why are you so restless and sighing?" The Righteous Man Wang was only thinking about his own business and did not answer her.

Madam Wang asked again, "What is the matter?"

The Righteous Man Wang said, "It is not something that you women can handle."

Madam Wang said, "Don't underestimate me just because I am a woman. Tell me what is the matter, and perhaps I can help you think of a way."

The Righteous Man Wang was at a loss. Hearing Madam Wang say this, he thought, "It would be good to have someone to discuss with." So he told her the reason why Xu Yuanbo and his wife had committed crimes, and that he wanted to save Mistress Xu.

Madam Wang said, "You admire Xu Yuanbo's righteousness and want to save his wife. That is what a real man would do. It would be great if we could find someone to go for Mistress Xu."

The Righteous Man Wang said, "Yes! But where to find such a chivalrous woman to suffer for Mistress Xu? That is what is troubling me."

Madam Wang listened, and remained silent. After a while, she said to the Righteous Man Wang in a serious manner, "I am willing to go for Mistress Xu. Saving people should be thorough. Saving Mistress Xu will also fulfill you. I am willing to go for Mistress Xu!"

The Righteous Man Wang never thought that his wife would give up her comfortable life and go to suffer for others. But this was too difficult. He still did not quite believe it, so he asked Madam Wang, "Are you telling the truth, or are you just joking?"

Madam Wang said, "Who is joking? I am really willing to go for Mistress Xu. You can be a real man, can't I be a female hero?"

The Righteous Man Wang quickly turned over and got out of bed, kneeling on the ground and saying, "Virtuous wife! You are truly a heroine. You have fulfilled me!"

Madam Wang also quickly got out of bed, kneeling on the ground and saying, "We are all doing this to save good people, to save those who are wronged. Why do you have to be like this?"

Immediately, the Righteous Man Wang went to the prison, brought Mistress Xu out, and went home with her. After sitting down, the Righteous Man Wang explained that he admired Xu Yuanbo, wanted to save her, and that Madam Wang was willing to go into exile for her.

Mistress Xu was very surprised and said, "My husband committed a crime, and I am exiled. It is all our fault. Not to mention suffering, even if I die, I should bear it. How can I trouble you, Madam! Absolutely not!"

The Righteous Man Wang said, "Mr. Xu is a loyal and righteous man. Who in the county doesn't sigh? If I don't save the wife of such a person, who else should I save? Madam, don't refuse. My wife and I have already discussed it."

Mistress Xu said, "Absolutely not! Even if you, Madam, are willing, I will feel uneasy! Absolutely not!"

Madam Wang said, "I have already made up my mind. Madam, whether you want to or not, that's how it will be!"

Mistress Xu saw that the Righteous Man Wang and Madam Wang were so determined and had no choice but to cry and bow to the ground, saying, "Thank you both for your kindness. I can only repay you in the next life!"

The Righteous Man Wang immediately sent Mistress Xu to her parents' home and hid her.

Madam Wang took Mistress Xu's name and went into exile. She endured countless hardships and sufferings along the way. It took her several months and she walked thousands of miles to finally arrive. Afterwards, the people of Rugao County all admired the righteousness of the couple. Everyone pooled together a sum of money and went to the place where Madam Wang was exiled to redeem her. The Righteous Man Wang and his wife were reunited again.

Benjamin Franklin (1706-1790) 206

— Li Jizhen

Undeterred by lightning during thunderstorms, he experimented with electricity. Over seventy years old, he journeyed across the ocean to plead for his people.

Benjamin Franklin was born in Boston, America, on January 17, 1706. His father was a dyer, originally from England, who immigrated to America. When he first arrived in America, he already had seven children. After his wife died, he remarried and had six more. Franklin was the youngest of his sons. Franklin's mother was kind and capable, very good at disciplining her children, creating a harmonious atmosphere of parental love, filial piety, brotherly affection, and fraternal respect.

At the age of eight, Franklin was sent to a village school by his parents. At that time, America was just a British colony, culturally backward, with no higher education institutions, only a few village schools teaching basic reading and arithmetic. Franklin, upon entering the school, realized that studying was not easy, and worked hard, achieving excellent results. His father, seeing his son's understanding, happily said, "This son of mine will surely become a pastor." Because pastors at that time were very knowledgeable and respected, he had such expectations for his beloved son. Unfortunately, due to the large family size and limited income, his father's financial situation worsened day by day, and he could not afford to support his son's education. After two years in the village school, Franklin was forced to drop out and work as a child laborer making soap and candles with his father. There, he paid attention to everything and gained much experience.

One day, his father took him to Boston for business. He saw the prosperity of various industries, with everyone diligently working in their respective fields. He was deeply moved and said to his father, "Dad! I like this hopeful city of Boston. I want to stay here and learn a trade. Dad, will you agree?" At this time, Franklin's brother, Jacob, had opened a printing house in Boston. Hearing Franklin's words, his father could not bear to refuse him and sent him to this printing house to learn printing. Franklin worked and studied, asking questions about everything he was unsure of, learning everything with great humility and diligence, and his studies progressed rapidly.

Jacob was a jealous and stingy person. Not only did he not cherish his good brother, but he also mistreated him severely. Franklin worked for Jacob for seven years, and Jacob did not give him a single penny of wages. Jacob was also worried that Franklin would not be willing to be his slave for life, so he took precautions and notified the nearby printing houses not to hire his brother. Initially, Franklin thought that his brother was just stricter than others and did not suspect any malicious intent. Later, he discovered all of his brother's treacherous schemes. He was disappointed and determined to leave. So, he quietly sold all his belongings, took the little money he had, and ran to New York, three hundred miles away. There, he had no reliable relatives or friends, and could not find a job as a printer. He went without a full meal for several days.

One afternoon, he was wandering the streets, hungry and desolate, trying to find a place to work, when he suddenly saw an advertisement from a printing house in Philadelphia seeking workers. He considered this a savior and immediately prepared to go. After struggling there for several years, he managed to make a living. While running the printing business, he also engaged in scientific research. Soon, he invented the copperplate and the stove. At this time, he had become an important figure in society. After gaining his own position, he remembered the difficulty of his early education and therefore paid great attention to public education, first running a newspaper and a library. Later, he was afraid that this would not be enough to thoroughly benefit the people, so he entered politics. At the age of seventy, he crossed the Atlantic twice to England to request the abolition of the Stamp Act for the American people, but unfortunately, he failed. He had to abandon his political life and concentrate on studying electricity, changing his approach to benefit the people. At that time, the American people truly lived up to him. Their petitions were ineffective, so they armed themselves and resisted, seceding from Britain to establish independence, creating a great power later on. After American independence, he once left the laboratory to represent the American people, lobbying various countries to seek recognition. He first moved France to recognize them, and other countries followed without objection. He was a great founding father of the United States.

Franklin began studying electricity very early on. After years of meticulous experiments, he officially invented "electricity" in 1752. That year, one day, dark clouds gathered, and thunder and lightning roared. He believed this was the best opportunity for him to experiment with extracting electricity from the clouds. He immediately put down everything he was doing and prepared for the experiment. He first used a piece of silk to make a kite, inserted a foot-long iron wire, then tied a string to it, and launched it into the clouds. He also tied an iron key wrapped in silk ribbon to the end of the string. Because silk does not conduct electricity, holding the iron key through the silk would prevent electrocution and death. He waited for a while, but besides the thunder in the sky becoming louder, there was no reaction. He doubted his procedure and was very anxious. Seeing the flashing lightning in the sky, he wished he could reach out and grab it. Just as he was extremely disappointed, a heavy rain suddenly poured down, completely soaking his clothes. He shivered constantly in the rain, but he did not retreat. He thought to himself, "If the electricity experiment cannot succeed, what is there to cherish about the body? If I cannot find any answers today, let the thunder and rain destroy me! I do not plan to go back..." Just as he thought of this, the string below the kite, which was originally very slack because it had been soaked by the rain, suddenly tightened, and sparks constantly flew from the iron key in his hand. He was not afraid at all. He looked at the lightning in the sky and then at the sparks in his hand, and happily said, "Electricity, I have indeed invented you. Before, I said that electricity could be extracted from the clouds, and lightning could be avoided, but all the great scholars in the world laughed at me for 'daydreaming.' Now, I have finally proven it! It shows that if people are willing to work hard for the truth, they will definitely not fail to achieve results."

Although he discovered electric sparks, he was not complacent and satisfied. He was unwilling to take the kite back to change his clothes. He shivered and speculated about the wet kite string: "Why didn't it conduct electricity at first, and only conducted electricity after being wet by the rain? Is it that the string itself does not conduct electricity, but becomes conductive when wet by water?" Later, after careful research, he learned that there are electrically conductive ions in rainwater, so the string can conduct electricity when wet (because carbon dioxide in the air dissolves in rainwater to form carbonic acid, and carbonic acid decomposes to produce positive and negative ions. These positive and negative ions can conduct electricity. Even water itself can decompose to produce positive and negative ions, but the amount is very small.)

Since Franklin invented electricity, later scientists have been able to use his electricity and his principles of electricity to invent telephones, telegraphs, electric lights, trams... for the benefit of the world. The benefits he gave to humanity are truly unparalleled.

Submission Guidelines 207

This journal accepts unsolicited manuscripts. We welcome historical stories, scientific invention stories, and modern knowledge stories. Upon acceptance, we will pay four yuan per thousand characters.

Manuscripts should not exceed 5,000 characters, with 2,000 to 3,000 characters being the most appropriate.

Manuscripts must be written in vernacular Chinese, striving for clarity, fluency, and accessibility, and avoiding Europeanized sentence structures.

Please send manuscripts to our office at Yenching University, Peiping.

Publishing World

How to Cultivate an Academic Atmosphere (Part 1) 208

— Zhou Hanmei

If we examine the current situation in China, the shallowness of the academic atmosphere is an undeniable fact. Whether in families, schools, or society in general, during leisure time, there is only low-level entertainment, with no proper cultivation of virtue; during work, there is only a decadent philosophy of opportunism, scheming, and infighting, with no diligent research from an academic or work perspective. This phenomenon pervades ordinary families and occupational groups. Even in most large and small schools, it is the same, with no distinction between superiors and inferiors. Therefore, assuming that the shallowness of China's academic atmosphere is due to the lack of basic education is a misguided assessment. The general truth of China is that people do not want academics, rather than desiring to study but being unable to. We should pay serious attention to this point. The author believes that the formation of this phenomenon has its own cause and effect. Therefore, to hope to cultivate a national academic atmosphere, we must start from its root cause.

Why do people serving in professional lines not need to study academics? Because they did not get this position entirely relying on their knowledge and talent, but rather relying on direct or indirect personal relationships. At the same time, maintaining this position and even promoting their position also does not entirely rely on their knowledge and talent, but rather relies on their ability to maneuver. We often hear people say, "The essence of dealing with people lies in 'feng ma niu'." If the secret of life is 'feng ma niu', then what is the need for academics? The author had a friend studying engineering abroad who studied for five full years overseas, mortgaging almost all of his family property, but failing to attain a high position after graduation. He interned in foreign factories for five or six years. He originally did not want to return to his home country, because he knew that his home country only needed 'feng ma niu' and did not need hard-working people. But his friends admonished him with great righteousness, believing that he should serve his home country and should not contribute his talents in a foreign country. This overseas student was repeatedly urged by his friends, and he returned home with his luggage. Unfortunately, this Chinese overseas student, who only knew how to study academics and did not understand human relationships, ended up dying in poverty and illness in a hostel in his home country. We certainly cannot say that there is not a trace of justice in Chinese society, but at least what pervades Chinese society in general is personal connections, and there is little guarantee of a livelihood based on academics. What a terrible phenomenon this is! Thus, fathers and elder brothers often admonish their children and younger brothers to be familiar with human relationships, and the children and younger brothers encourage themselves to deeply study 'feng ma niu'. The whole world is like this, and human desires are rampant. How can we still talk about whether the academic atmosphere is shallow or not?

A New Era of Popular Reading 209

— Chen Gaoyong

"National Novel Series" Published by Zhengzhong Book Company

Recently, Zhengzhong Book Company, in order to promote social education and meet the needs of the public, specially commissioned many experts to compile two series of National Novels, a total of one hundred volumes. The content is divided into ten collections: 1. History Collection, 2. Revolution Collection, 3. Geography Collection, 4. Famous Biography Collection, 5. Health Collection, 6. Production and Economics Collection, 7. Politics Collection, 8. Defense Collection, 9. Science Collection, 10. Life Collection. Using the style of chapter novels, it narrates various knowledge that is truly relevant to the people. Anyone who has studied for one or two years can easily read it and develop interest. This is indeed a great contribution to social education! A friend sent me the fifty volumes that have already been published, which gave me many thoughts after reading them.

I remember when the so-called drum song master Liu Baoquan came to Shanghai half a month ago, one night a friend and I went to listen to Liu tell stories. Liu's opening remarks after taking the stage said: "The material for storytelling, no matter who it is, is nothing more than 'Romance of the Three Kingdoms', 'Dream of the Red Chamber', 'Romance of the West Chamber', 'Water Margin', and other novels. If you leave these novels, then no one can sing or tell stories, so past and present, it's nothing more than stories of heroes and beauties." At that time, I had a question after hearing this: Why can't we compile stories about things that are closely related to modern times and the public as material for storytelling? Why is it still using a few old novels as the only material even today? What help do these outdated stories give to the current actual life of the general public? If we compiled many events in history, such as Lin Zexu banning opium, Zeng Guofan suppressing Hong Yang, the Boxer Rebellion, the Eight-Nation Alliance attacking Beijing, the Wuxu Reform, the Huanghuagang Uprising, the Xinhai Revolution, and the Northern Expedition of the National Revolutionary Army, into interesting stories as material for storytelling, wouldn't it be more meaningful for the general public to listen to?

We also often see in the newspapers that some young people in various places read absurd and unbelievable supernatural novels and believe them to be true, so they hide it from their parents and siblings, and flee together to some mountain to seek gods and learn swordsmanship. We should never always say that these young people have simple minds and immature thoughts; in fact, the influence of so-called popular novels on people is too profound. When young people are in the prime of their desire for knowledge, and there is no proper reading material to meet their needs, they have no choice but to read supernatural novels.

Let's look at the plays performed in several theaters in Shanghai recently. It's either "Burning the Red Lotus Temple", or "Journey to the West", or else something like "Pan Jinlian and Widow Ma's Inn", nothing but gods and monsters, or lewdness, and they can actually be full every day, with one play running for a month or two without stopping. And most of the audience are petty citizens who fundamentally lack modern knowledge, so the impact is such that the results are truly unspeakable.

From these things, we cannot but say that the public life in China is too dangerous, and social education in China is too lacking. If we want to revitalize the nation at this moment, we first need to modernize our country. If we want to modernize our country, we must first modernize the thinking of the people. If we want to modernize the thinking of the people, we must pay great attention to social education. The work of social education is of course multifaceted, and compiling a kind of popular reading material suitable for the times is currently the most needed work.

We know that for many years, the authority that has dominated our social public is not the Bible or sage texts, but rather a few popular novels; not Confucius, Mencius, Zhu Xi, Wang Yangming and others, but rather Kongming, Guan Yu, Song Jiang, Wu Song and others. The so-called "Romance of the Three Kingdoms", "Water Margin", "Dream of the Red Chamber", and other popular novels, although they still have their literary value today, their content is already somewhat incompatible with the lives of the general public today. Therefore, if we want to enable the public to obtain a basic knowledge that adapts to modern life, and cultivate a lifestyle that adapts to modern society, we must have a new reading material that is easily accepted by the public. The National Novel Series of Zhengzhong Book Company can be said to have been compiled in response to this need.

In recent years, more and more people have been paying attention to popular reading materials, such as the collection of folk songs from various places, and the textual research of various folk legends, which are often seen in newspapers and magazines. However, this kind of collection and textual research work is useful for people who study learning, but not very useful for the general public with shallow knowledge. For example, if we investigate the evolution process of the story of Xiao Chu Xu Wenchang, people who study history and literature can know the evolution of a legend, and develop great interest, but the general public who only knows how to read has no such research interest at all. Therefore, for popular reading materials, on the one hand, we need scholars with deep thoughts to collect and research for us to serve as research data, and on the other hand, we also need people with fluent writing skills to systematically edit them for the public to read. The compilation of the National Novel Series should meet the needs of the public.

I have read through the fifty volumes of National Novel Series that have already been published, and I feel that there are the following points that can be praised:

It adopts the genre of chapter novels, so that a fact is connected from beginning to end, forming a complete and systematic story, which is exactly what those who are used to reading old chapter novels like.

The narration is simple and clear, without the excessive elaboration of old novels, so that people with a shallow level of knowledge can easily understand and remember.

It transforms specialized scientific knowledge into concrete stories, so that readers can unknowingly gain a lot of scientific knowledge while reading the stories.

It turns ideal things into realistic stories, so that people feel that many beautiful lives can be obtained in reality, and people unknowingly tend towards a reasonable life.

The above four points are the points that I personally feel satisfied with after reading them. I very much hope that people who are enthusiastic about social education will continue to compile more popular reading materials like this. I also hope that literate citizens who have studied for one or two years will save the time and money they spend listening to storytelling and reading comic books, and buy some of these kinds of reading materials as spiritual food.

Finally, I would like to offer a reading experience from my past as a reference for those who compile and purchase this kind of book. I remember when I was in elementary school, the Commercial Press was publishing a series of books for young people, which contained stories of famous people from China and abroad, with simple words and pure content. The books were small and cheap. I bought one book every week as extracurricular reading. After reading more than twenty books, my thinking was greatly influenced, and I didn't even want to read "Water Margin" and "Dream of the Red Chamber" anymore. Today, the Young People's Series has become an outdated thing, but the influence I have received has not disappeared, while the so-called "Dream of the Red Chamber", which was once popular, I still have not fully read. Therefore, I very much hope that the influence of the National Novel Series on the general literate public will be the same as the influence of the Young People's Series on me personally.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Commentary

Is This the Gentleman's Demeanor of England? 210

— Xing An

Seeing the incident of the British Consul in Yunnan, Harding, committing assault without reason, and injuring a training officer of the school's Boy Scouts, really makes people feel very indignant! According to the Kunming telegram from the Central News Agency, the Boy Scouts of the Provincial Commercial School were going to visit the British Garden. They stopped in front of the gate and first instructed the gatekeeper to report inside. At that time, the British Consul Harding happened to be in the garden. Upon hearing the news, he brought out two hunting dogs. Then, three Boy Scout training officers went forward to state their intentions. Unexpectedly, Harding, with a fierce demeanor, without distinguishing right from wrong, without saying a word, immediately used his cane to beat the people indiscriminately, and cursed loudly. His hunting dogs were also eager to bite. All three people who were beaten were seriously injured.

From the course of this incident, it can be seen that this British Consul Harding's act of assaulting people is truly tyrannical to the extreme! The school's Boy Scouts wanted to visit the British Garden. They stopped in front of the gate and first instructed the gatekeeper to report inside, which is not comparable to those who enter without permission. If Harding looked down on Chinese students, or had other reasons for not allowing outsiders to visit, he could have refused. But he suddenly showed off his power, brought out two hunting dogs, with a fierce demeanor, without distinguishing right from wrong, without saying a word, and used his cane to beat the people indiscriminately and cursed loudly. This kind of rude behavior really goes against the identity of a consul. Does Harding view the fact that Chinese school Boy Scouts want to visit the British Garden as an insult to the dignity of the British? Or was he just drunk at the time, so his actions were so abnormal? However, according to Harding's defense to our country's negotiators, he said that his assault was a proper disposition. Randomly beating and cursing people is still considered a proper disposition. What exactly is the logic behind this?

Incidents of foreigners in China assaulting Chinese people without reason have been heard from time to time. Not long ago, an American sailor assaulting a Chinese person case occurred in Shanghai. Now, a Boy Scout training officer from a school in Yunnan Province has been assaulted by this British Consul Harding. But in the past, most of the people who committed the assaults were foreigners without status. But this time, the person who committed the assault was the British Consul, who is a diplomat. This is what makes us unable not to be astonished! Moreover, it is said that Harding has a violent temperament and has committed assaults many times in Yunnan. Such a diplomat truly goes against the dignity of England. England is known as a nation of gentlemen. Is this the gentleman's demeanor of England?

After Watching "Lady Windermere's Fan" 211

— Li Yi

Performed by the China Traveling Theater at the Carlton

Following "Thunderstorm", "La Traviata", and "Melody Lane", we also saw the China Traveling Theater's "Lady Windermere's Fan."

At this time of national crisis, especially in

Page 18

In the difficult month of May, staging plays like "La Traviata" already made us feel that the plays were too soft; and now, they are staging this outdated "Lady Windermere's Fan." Coming from North China, the China Traveling Theater, has it forgotten the current situation in North China that it witnessed and experienced?

What do we see in an outdated play like "Lady Windermere's Fan"? It is the depraved and boring lives of the gentlemen and ladies of the upper class, those games of love...

If exposing the depraved and boring lives of the upper class and adding severe criticism is originally not impossible. But "Lady Windermere's Fan" is obviously not like that. Here, drinking, playing cards, talking about women, and opening dance parties are only used as decorations for upper-class figures. It is a kind of praise rather than criticism. Even if there is some so-called subtle satire, it is only subtle satire. Its function is originally the same as a familiar friend saying "haha" and making a joke.

But unfortunately, "Lady Windermere's Fan" is not just a "haha". There are even greater toxins behind it—

A woman abandoning her child and eloping behind her husband's back is not a terrible crime, in my opinion. Of course, running away after losing a husband who "loves" her and her lovely children is a very big sacrifice in private relationship. If the new object plays with it for a while and then throws it away, it will be even more unfortunate; However, I still do not give Nora much sympathy for her departure, and I think that she is right to go? So, a character like Xu Ziming is not much better than Lord Windermere, although the one who encouraged her to elope is the same as Xu Ziming.

Ms. Jin advises her daughter, Xu Shaonai, to return to her husband's arms, which may be right in a certain sense, but what is she advised to go back to do? To be a new virtuous wife and loving mother. She is only advised not to lose her original master, who treats her very well, like her, if she loses her original master who treats her very well (?), she will end up "wandering and destitute, with a bad reputation".

This is just advising people to compromise with the old and not resist! The new will not be better than the old!

Although it is said that Liu Boying in "Lady Windermere's Fan" will not be better than Xu Ziming, it may be a fact, and Xu Shaonai has no ability to do anything other than be a "toy wife". However, what are the audience under the stage considered to be?

What kind of preaching is this!

As for the performance, the stage design is quite beautiful. Among the actors' acting skills, Jiang Ming's Ba Daren is the most popular (I hope he can reduce some of his anger). Tang Ruoqing and Zhang Manping performed very steadily. Dai Ya's Xu Ziming is very suave in his movements, but his voice is too old, perhaps because he is used to playing old people; Tao Jin's Liu Boying is not enough, and Tan Wen's Zhang Yizhi also performed too exaggeratedly.

Death (Continued) 212

— Black Ding

He still wanted to say more. He looked up and saw me standing nearby. Immediately, he looked embarrassed, left the bed, approached me, and whispered, "Oh, you, when did you get back?"

Before I could answer him, suddenly, my relative, as if unable to bear it, loudly interrupted, "Think about it yourself, you come here again and again, and every time you say you want to improve, have you improved? When you can't afford opium, you shoot morphine, you inhale heroin. You, at such a young age, don't want to be a human being. You've sold the house and land. You tricked your wife and children into going to Lushun, and you hardened your heart and sold them. You still have the nerve to come back and say they abandoned you..."

I sadly looked at the window.

He was scolded by his uncle and burst into tears. He tugged at my clothes and said, "I really want to quit this time, but I have no money, alas..."

After speaking to me, he looked at his uncle timidly with pitiful eyes. Like a child, he wiped away his tears with his hand and said, "Just this once, give me some money, and I'll never come to you again..."

Finally, his uncle took out eight dimes from his pocket and placed them in his hand. He looked satisfied, walked out the door, braved the rain in the dark night, and disappeared into a grove of trees.

Unexpectedly, three days later, he was brought back by two policemen with his hands tied behind his back, again looking for his uncle. As soon as he entered the house, he knelt before his uncle, crying and begging, "Brother, brother, I'm so wronged. I was implicated by someone. They said I stole something that someone else stole... Please write me a guarantee so I can get out."

His uncle pushed him out the door.

The two policemen kept slapping him in the face and loudly cursing, "You motherfucker, you said you had someone to vouch for you, but they pushed you out the door... Go, go, go back to jail..."

Half a month later, it was heard that he had died in prison.

The Tiger's Mouth 213

— Lin Hao

The vast sky was a milky white, as if smeared with a layer of gray. The fiery red morning sun reflected a few sparse morning stars, making them appear even dimmer. The lapping of the water sparkled with hundreds of silver snakes, making it hard to open one's eyes. In such a morning scene, apart from occasionally hearing a few croaking sounds of frogs, it was difficult to hear other sounds. Everything quietly slept in the embrace of tranquility. Even the few fishing boats by the sea were as silent and peaceful as if there was no one on board.

Toot! ——

But that sound startled everything. The fishermen abruptly woke from their dreams, touched their dirty, oily faces, stretched, and the croaking of the frogs became noticeably louder, incessantly chattering. In the forest, the little birds chirped and hummed. The gentle breeze blew through the grass, as if amplifying the sound waves a bit. …Thus, the sea surface became as lively as if it had transformed into something entirely different.

Toot! —— The sound seemed to come from something black emitting smoke. While shaking the ship's body with a "hong ya hong," it went——Toot! ——Toot!

This time, Grandfather Shun was raising money for the village to build a wall. Everyone in the village was penniless; who could afford to pay for the wall? Fortunately, someone in Shanghai had made a fortune, so Grandfather Shun dutifully took the donation book and went to raise money, collecting nearly a hundred foreign coins—no, it should be national currency now—and happily boarded the ship back. At this moment, he stared blankly at the white bubbles on the water, lost in thought, chewing on a vague memory:

It was sometime ago that a feng shui master had visited Shijia Village. According to his conclusion after surveying the surroundings of Shijia Village, the feng shui of Jinjia Village was indeed excellent, but unfortunately, it could not withstand the tiger's mouth of the Jinjia Ancestral Hall. It was like a tangerine with only a little bit of rot, perhaps harboring endless future troubles. It would be best to build a wall in front of the ancestral hall to block the tiger's mouth. Otherwise…

But who would believe it? Shijia Village had once experienced a period of prosperity. They dismissed the feng shui master's unreasonable and absurd words as a gentle breeze by their ears, rolling their eyes at him. Seeing that he seemed to be a hopeless case, he staggered away.

However, Shijia Village had indeed been acting strangely lately. The clan elder Ying died. The nimble Sister-in-law A Long, the honest A Qing, A Fu... they all died suddenly! What was left? People like Rongfa, Houfa, A Shui, A Bing... were all rogues, nothing but strong and overbearing fellows who only cared about eating. Under these circumstances, Shijia Village declined day by day.

Toot!—— The ship arrived at the dock, cutting off Grandfather Shun's thoughts.

Back home, he eagerly prepared to open the ancestral hall for a meeting.

Things became difficult. The farmland in front of the ancestral hall happened to belong to Uncle A Chang, who was a notorious skinflint. His mind was filled with selfishness. He didn't care about anything. As for attending this meeting, he was there because he thought his land might be sold for a higher price.

"Is that so? Uncle A Chang, you don't need to worry about the money. Now, we just need you to allow four fen of land, just four fen is enough. We'll buy it from you, and then we can start construction."

Of course, Uncle A Chang quoted a shocking price. And A Shui stood up abruptly from the bench:

"Uncle A Chang, that's not gold land either. No outsider is as black-hearted as you. Think about it, we're doing this for everyone. You should also fulfill some obligations, right?"

Uncle A Chang just smiled coldly, moved his lips, raised a hand like a twig, stroked his mustache, and coldly said nothing.

Bang! It was Houfa who slammed the table and roared:

"What's the point of talking to such an unreasonable person? Grandfather Shun, you quickly find a way to handle this. If anything goes wrong... Hey! Uncle A Chang, you hear me, everyone heard me, this is Houfa speaking. If I go back on my word, I'll be a son of a bitch. Understand? You tell me."

"That's right! Grandfather Shun, you do your thing. Are you afraid he won't agree?" A Shui also raised his fist and banged it on the table.

So, A Bing, Rongfa, A Dong... one by one, they made a commotion. Uncle A Chang finally yielded to an extremely low price in an extremely tense atmosphere.

Soon, a short, whitewashed wall was built in front of the Shijia Ancestral Hall. From then on, the people of Shijia Village could no longer see that terrifying tiger's mouth.

However, Shijia Village continued to decline day by day...

Immortal Zhang 214

— Yan

Zhang Er of Huangzhen is now respectfully called Immortal Zhang.

Huangzhen hasn't had a good harvest for three years. Old Man Liu San, who sits in the teahouse every day, grumbles that because there hasn't been a temple fair for three years, this is retribution. In the end, he blames the young people: "Those young fellows, where did they hear those wild rumors? If they continue to destroy temples, Huangzhen will turn into a land of hungry ghosts."

In fact, the young people also respected and believed in General Meng, but for three years, the fields haven't yielded enough, and the granaries are pressing hard to collect rent. After a year of hard work, they still have empty stomachs. What spare money do they have to honor General Meng with a procession in a red silk sedan chair? General Meng is powerful and should bless Huangzhen with several bumper harvests, pay off the debts, and fill their stomachs. Everyone would happily put on a three-day temple fair. But as soon as spring arrived, there wasn't a single grain in the pot, and the capital for planting hadn't been secured. It was truly a dream for General Meng to ride in a red silk sedan chair. The young people drank a little wine and thought about destroying General Meng's temple, letting them destroy themselves, and letting Huangzhen die clean!

Old Man Liu San was, after all, old: "Don't act rashly. General Meng certainly doesn't know that there hasn't been a good harvest for three years. He hasn't gone on patrol, so how would he know the condition of the fields? Somehow, everyone scrape together some money for a small temple fair. When General Meng sees this situation, he will surely show great compassion, and this year will be a good harvest..."

These words were what everyone longed for in their hearts, so they scraped together a sum of money, and General Meng was carried out of the temple.

That day, the faces of the men were filled with smiles, like a good sun after a rainy day. They casually cleaned up the temple, which was covered with spiderwebs. General Meng was invited out of the shrine. The person in charge of the invitation was naturally Old Man Liu San. When he helped General Meng into the sedan chair, he silently prayed in his heart, "General Meng, Huangzhen is too poor. There hasn't been a good harvest for three years. The sedan chair hasn't been replaced with new red silk. I beg General Meng to bestow blessings, to bring a five-shi harvest this year (an ordinary mu of land can yield three shi of grain; five shi is a great harvest). Next year, we'll gild him and decorate him, and put on a three-day opera." He bowed his head deeply, touching his forehead to the cold floor tiles. The men and children of Huangzhen, as long as they were male, fell down behind Old Man Liu San like logs, each with a desire in their heart, silently praying, a dream of a five-shi bumper harvest floating in everyone's mind.

Outside the door, a cannon sounded, and everyone cheered and stood up. Four men grabbed General Meng's sedan chair and rushed out. Those people followed behind, but they couldn't catch up with the sedan chair. Only when the sedan chair had circled every field bank in Huangzhen and returned to the temple did everyone follow back to kowtow. Then, the person in charge of the invitation helped General Meng back into the shrine.

This year, because of the path-clearing ceremony, the four men carrying the sedan chair, driven by the dream of five shi, carried it back to the temple as if their eight legs had wings. But when Old Man Liu San wanted to help General Meng into the shrine, he discovered that a person was sleeping in the shrine, with white foam at the corner of his mouth and his eyes slanted in the corners, as if he had died.

It was Zhang San, a good-for-nothing character in Huangzhen who, after gambling and eating away the few mu of land left by his ancestors, wandered everywhere.

"You wretch! You wretch!" Old Man Liu San scolded.

The men carried Zhang San down. He woke up, opened his eyes wide, and said in a foreign accent, "What are you doing! I know Huangzhen hasn't had a good harvest for three years. You kindly invited me to go on patrol. I promise you'll have a five-shi harvest this year."

The men were stunned. But Old Man Liu San immediately had a flash of inspiration. He knew that General Meng had possessed Zhang San's body. He knelt down with a thud and kowtowed repeatedly. The men immediately fell to the ground like logs again, shouting about the power of General Meng.

When Zhang San woke up, he was almost scared to jump up. He wanted to escape out the door. Old Man Liu San held him down and told him that General Meng had possessed his body and wanted him to live in the temple from now on. General Meng still had words to be conveyed through him.

Page 19

Page 20

Page 21

So Zhang San was respectfully called Immortal Zhang. He lived in the temple, receiving food and clothing from the people of Huangzhen. When he went out, he swaggered and received the kowtows of the crowd. When someone in the town was sick or had some difficulty, they would go to Immortal Zhang. He would immediately slant his eyes into the corners, foam at the mouth, speak in a foreign accent, say some medicine names, and think of ways to help them.

But a month later, Immortal Zhang disappeared. Old Man Liu San ordered the men to search everywhere. They found him in a gambling den in a neighboring town. He was happily talking about his act of playing a god. He boasted about his clothes, his money, and that he was now a very rich man.

Zhang San was carried back to Huangzhen by the men, beaten half to death. The men's dream of five shi had been shattered. They wanted to vent the resentment of not having a good harvest for three years on Zhang San. That night, they tied Zhang San to General Meng's shrine and set it on fire.

After that, Old Man Liu San, who sat in the teahouse, silently chewed on his dry tobacco pipe…

Drama 216

The Locked Box

Weige Di, the wife of the farmer Sorld, sits in the house embroidering. It must be nearly dusk! At this time, the bright sunset shines through the window and strokes the embroidery, arousing Weige Di's endless reveries...

"My lover drowned in Laojian, Laolan! I originally wanted to forget you forever"...

She uncontrollably uttered a moving dirge.

Naturally, when her husband returned, he didn't like hearing such a song.

Sorld said she was "meowing."

Sorld came back from the fair in disappointment, looking unusually irritable and embarrassed. It seemed like everything offended him.

Ah! He tiredly lay straight down on a box to rest, waiting for his wife to prepare dinner.

He had heard a murder case from the crowd at the fair.

A man named Hao Er was stabbed to death on the beach. The person who killed Hao Er was Solov, his welcome cousin.

While the two were talking about how pitiful the murderer would be, Wiege Di hoped that her cousin hadn't killed Hao Er....... At that moment, a voice came from outside the door: "Do good, save me!"

It was the murderer Solov who came in, panting... He refused to let his cousin kiss him. He thought that his cousin would not recognize him as her cousin because she knew that he was the one who killed Hao Er.

However, his cousin didn't mind at all.

Naturally, since they were both human, why should Solov be bullied by Hao Er? In Solov's opinion, killing Hao Er was a fair fight.

Now, he asked his cousin to hide him for a night or two. But his cousin was a woman, and she thought that "women are not suitable for doing such things." But after all, because they were siblings, she hid him in the sheep pen.

In contrast, Sorld was afraid of this matter. He worried that hiding Solov would be disadvantageous to him. He was simply afraid to the point of crying. He knew how Hao Er's brother Angel would come to search his house, which would put his own life in danger....

Should she really watch her cousin – Solov, who might be in imminent danger - and not save him? She despised her husband's courage.

However, Angel finally came knocking urgently on the door.

Angel forced Wiege Di to step aside.

After some insistence, Sorld, who had been afraid to the point of crying, sold Solov out to Angel for three silver marks.

This made Wiege Di truly anxious. While they were all upstairs, she quickly locked her cousin in the box.

How could they let this go? We will have to see the wisdom of this brave cousin.

Listen, Wiege Di will give you a very satisfactory answer.

Movie News

YMCA 9th Floor 218

Reception Banquet for Three Pairs of Artists Performances with wonderful jokes

Tang Na, Lan Ping; Zhao Dan, Ye Luqian; Gu Eryi, Du Mingjie; After these three pairs of artists returned from their weddings in Hangzhou, they hosted a reception for relatives and friends at the YMCA in Baxianqiao last night (the 5th). At this tea party, it was truly a gathering of stars and artists. There was endless excitement and interesting stories. Now, let's put aside the main topic and record some anecdotes below, so that those who did not participate in the event can also know some of the "artistic sentiments" of that time on paper. (Using old Teng's language)

Shen "Monster" Xiling, who originally taught in Guangxi, came to Shanghai on official business and happened to participate in the grand event. This gentleman, who came from the southern country of Erythrina red beans, brought many red beans (this object is the most reminiscent of love). At the banquet, whenever he met a friend, he would give each person two, to express his feelings of longing.

Someone, not knowing who, said that red beans could be eaten. Jiang Dongliang couldn't wait to swallow the red beans into his mouth. At that time, someone happened to be reciting the poem "Red beans grow in the southern country," and when they recited the last line, "this object is the most reminiscent of love," they pointed at Mr. Jiang, causing the whole hall to burst into laughter.

While this side was having a good time, old Teng dragged Ling Hefu to see Chen Bowan to introduce them. He himself pretended that he didn't know either of them, performing with great skill and appearing to have the talent of a comedian.

The master of ceremonies, Mr. Shi Chao, had to not only raise his voice to announce the program but also ask the guest representatives to ask the bride and groom to report on their love stories. He performed in all aspects and with many jokes, winning the support of the guests.

The seats were arranged very well, in pairs. For example, Hu Die and Pan Yousheng were a pair, Chen Wanli and Wu Mei were another pair, and Wang Ying and Jin Shan were also arranged together.

After the representative of the new couple, Dian Na, gave a speech, it was the guests' turn to speak. Ouyang Yuqian was chosen as the representative. Mr. Ouyang bombed as soon as he came on stage, reducing the three pairs of newlyweds to two pairs (perhaps on purpose). As soon as he said the words, he knew he had made a mistake and immediately corrected himself, but it had already caused the whole audience to laugh uncontrollably. The gist of his speech was: "In such an unfree environment, there is actually such a free union. And with such free air now, I am truly happy. In the future, I hope that the newlyweds and the guests will unite and seek freedom together in this unfree environment." (Later, Zhou Jianyun and others also gave speeches, with the same general meaning.)

After the guests gave their speeches, one of the newlyweds, Zhao Dan, returned from outside. Everyone asked him to speak. After he spoke, Gu Eryi was also pulled up. He was wearing a hat, and people asked him to take it off, but he was unwilling. Suddenly, Zheng Junli, like a tiger, darted out from the side, grabbed his hat, and ran away. This is how the truth was revealed. It turned out that he had recently shaved the hair on the top of his head for filming "Carnival Night," so "the bald man was afraid of taking off his hat."

After the grooms finished their speeches, naturally someone suggested that the brides should also say a few words. So the negotiation commissioner, Shi Chao, said, "Wait a minute, let me go and smooth things over." As a result, he did not fail in his mission, and the brides came out one by one to say to the guests, "I am truly happy today. I can't express how happy I am… Thank you all." Then they quickly turned around and fled into the lounge. When it was Ye Luqian's turn to finish speaking and step back, a friend suddenly struck a gong next to her. The sound of the gong was exactly the same as the adjutant's report in "The Imperial Envoy" that the real imperial envoy had arrived.

Unexpectedly, one wave subsided, and another rose. Mr. Zhou Jianyun raised a serious protest over there, saying, "They didn't hear the words of the bride and groom clearly and requested them to go to that end and say them again." This protest later came to nothing because someone else proposed that the newlyweds report on their love stories.

Again, after the negotiation of the negotiation commissioner Shi Chao, the three grooms came out to report on their love stories. Zhao Dan said, "Love between men and women is always so and so, that's all, that's all." Shi Chao said, "Since Zhao Dan said 'that's all, that's all,' we'll call 'that's all' to report."

"Iron Horse" Soviet Russia's Latest Amphibious Tank 219

He had already reported it more bluntly, saying, "I fell in love with her at first sight."

Tang Na said, "I love her, and she loves me."

Someone else suggested that Commissioner Shi Chao be asked to invite the bride out to report on their love story. Shi Chao gave the guests a hint, saying they were "over there" (in the women's restroom), and requested a female representative be sent to ask. The result was nothing came of it.

Next was the giving of gifts. Flowers were passed down each table, one by one, and whoever had the flower when the drum stopped would win a prize. The first group, starting with the middle table, winners were Zhang Yiping and Mao Yu! The second group, Chen Wanli; the third group, Xu Huaisha.

The first group's prizes were a small flower basket and two small umbrellas. While Mao Yu was playing with and admiring the small umbrella, Shu Xiuwen unexpectedly snatched it from behind. Mao Yu, being "young and handsome" and quick on his feet, dodged the attacker, but unexpectedly, the front door was blocked by a tiger, and the back door by a wolf. Qian Taisheng snatched it from that side. Qian Taisheng got the small umbrella, and Shu Xiuwen demanded it from him, resulting in a comedic scene of Qian Taisheng teasing Shu Xiuwen three times. In the end, it was still returned to Mao Yu.

Just as the music program was about to begin, Xu Suling suddenly suggested that Ouyang Yuqian be asked to sing Pan Jinlian; Hu Die be asked to sing "Night Fragrance"; and Old Teng be asked to give a speech.

Ouyang Yuqian said that his voice wasn't good and he couldn't sing. Moreover, the play "Pan Jinlian" might have sold well when I sang it ten years ago, but now Bai Yushuang should take the limelight.

Hu Die also couldn't sing because her throat had just recovered. As a result, only Old Teng came on stage and gave a speech with a rather "artistic" tone of "so, this, that."

It was getting late, and the music program began. It included Miss Lang Yuxiu's solo singing: "Serenade," "Three Grievances of the Rose," and a violin solo by a national music expert. Someone asked Miss Wang Ying to sing a Japanese song, but Wang Ying preemptively refused to sing.

Finally, everyone sang together the "Six Harmonies Wedding Song Congratulation Melody," with lyrics by Sun Shiyi and music by Ming Ji: "Amorous man, with bride, shadows paired beneath the Six Harmonies Pagoda; Victory in the field of love, do not forget the barbarians reaching the Yangtze River, do not forget the barbarians reaching the Yangtze River!" "Drink celebratory wine, create a joyous wedding chamber, the tide of May is high and the momentum is rising; Together go to the battlefield, together save China and recover Shenyang, together save China and recover Shenyang!"

It was reported to be eleven o'clock, and everyone dispersed happily.
